Most important [https://web.archive.org/web/20141106185805/http://s2.manifo.com/usr/f/f0b13/97/img/0beksport-europa.jpg importers of Poland's 2012 exports, graph.] Manifo ([[Wayback Machine|Wayback]]).</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.worldstopexports.com/polands-top-import-partners/|title=Poland's Top Trading Partners|first=Daniel|last=Workman|date=2 March 2019|website=World's Top Exports|access-date=27 March 2019}}</ref> In September 2018, the unemployment rate was estimated at 5.7%, one of the lowest in the European Union.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://businessinsider.com.pl/finanse/makroekonomia/bezrobocie-w-polsce-wrzesien-2018-r/437gjnh|title=GUS podał najnowsze dane dot. bezrobocia w Polsce|date=23 October 2018|access-date=28 October 2018}}</ref> In 2019, Poland passed a law that would exempt workers under the age of 26 from [[income tax]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/07/30/europe/poland-income-tax-youths-intl/index.html|title=Brain drain claimed 1.7 million youths. So this country is scrapping its income tax|author=Ivana Kottasová|website=CNN|date=30 July 2019|access-date=30 July 2019}}</ref>

[[File:Giełda Papierów Wartościowych w Warszawie ul. Książęca 2020.jpg|thumb|right|The [[Warsaw Stock Exchange]] is the largest exchange by market capitalization in [[East-Central Europe]].]]

The Polish banking sector is the largest in the region,<ref name="TWI-2011" /> with 32.3 branches per 100,000 adults.<ref>Worldbank.org, [http://siteresources.worldbank.org/EXTGLOBALFINREPORT/Resources/8816096-1361888425203/9062080-1364927957721/GFDR-2014_Statistical_Appendix_B.pdf Global Financial Development Report 2014.] Appendix B. Key Aspects of Financial Inclusion (PDF file, direct download). Retrieved 6 November 2014. There are 32.3 providers per 100,000 adults in Poland by IMF's Financial Access Survey (FAS). Comparatively, in the United States there are 35.4 but in Cyprus a whopping 103.9.</ref><ref name="datatopics/poland">World Bank, [http://datatopics.worldbank.org/financialinclusion/country/poland Financial Inclusion Data. Country Dashboard: Poland.] The World Bank Group. Retrieved 6 November 2014.</ref> The banks are the largest and most developed sector of the country's [[financial market]]s. They are regulated by the [[Financial Supervision Authority (Poland)|Polish Financial Supervision Authority]]. Poland's banking sector has approximately 5 national banks, a network of nearly 600 cooperative banks and 18 branches of foreign-owned banks. In addition, foreign investors have controlling stakes in nearly 40 commercial banks, which make up 68% of the banking capital.<ref name="TWI-2011">Thomas White International (September 2011), [https://web.archive.org/web/20130913074250/http://www.thomaswhite.com/global-perspectives/banking-sector-in-poland/ Prominent Banks in Poland.] Emerging Market Spotlight. Banking Sector in Poland (Internet Archive). Retrieved 6 November 2014.</ref>

Products and goods manufactured in Poland include: electronics, buses and trams ([[Solaris Bus & Coach|Solaris]], [[Solbus]]), helicopters and planes ([[PZL Świdnik]], [[PZL Mielec]]), trains ([[Pesa SA|Pesa]], [[Newag]]), ships ([[Gdańsk Shipyard]], [[Szczecin Shipyard]]), military equipment ([[FB "Łucznik" Radom]], [[:pl:Bumar Łabędy|Bumar-Łabędy]], [[Jelcz]]), medicines ([[:pl:Zakłady Farmaceutyczne Polpharma|Polpharma]], [[:pl:Polfa Warszawa|Polfa]]), food ([[Tymbark (company)|Tymbark]], [[Hortex]], [[E. Wedel]]), clothes ([[LPP (company)|LLP]]), glass, pottery ([[Boleslawiec Pottery|Bolesławiec]]), chemical products and others. Well-known brands and companies include [[Alior Bank]], [[PKN Orlen|Orlen]]&[[Grupa Lotos|Lotos Group]], [[Inglot Cosmetics]], [[Plus (telecommunications Poland)|Plus]], [[Play (telecommunications)|Play]], [[Brainly]], [[Netguru]], [[GOG.com]], [[CD Projekt]], [[Trefl]] and [[Allegro (website)|Allegro]]. Poland is also one of the world's biggest producers of [[copper]], [[silver]], [[coal]], furniture, automotive parts and [[soft drink]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://knaufautomotive.com/the-automotive-industry-in-poland-what-we-produce-and-who-are-our-customers/|title=The automotive industry in Poland &#124; Knauf Automotive|date=30 June 2020}}</ref><ref>https://industryeurope.com/poland-furniture-production-powerhouse/#:~:text=Poland%20is%20currently%20the%20fourth,furniture%2C%20after%20Germany%20and%20Italy {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201123163900/https://industryeurope.com/poland-furniture-production-powerhouse/#:~:text=Poland%20is%20currently%20the%20fourth,furniture%2C%20after%20Germany%20and%20Italy |date=23 November 2020 }}.</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.worldstopexports.com/top-soft-drinks-exporters-by-country/|title=Top Soft Drinks Exporters by Country|date=13 September 2020|website=World's Top Exports}}</ref>

=== Tourism ===
{{Main|Tourism in Poland|List of World Heritage Sites of Poland|List of Historic Monuments (Poland)|Seven Wonders of Poland|Crown of Polish Mountains}}
[[File:Ratusz Zamosc.jpg|thumb|left|The [[Zamość|Old City of Zamość]] is a [[UNESCO World Heritage Site]].]]
Poland experienced a significant increase in the number of tourists after joining the European Union in 2004.<ref name="Travel And Tourism in Poland" /><ref>{{Cite book|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=RrsdPZhIdlIC&q=polska+turystyka+unia+europejska&pg=PA102|title=Polska pięć lat w Unii Europejskiej|first=Stanisław|last=Konopacki|date=12 March 2009|publisher=WSMIP UŁ|isbn=978-83-88679-84-1|via=Google Books}}</ref> With nearly 21 million international arrivals in 2019, tourism contributes considerably to the overall economy and makes up a relatively large proportion of the country's service market.<ref name="unwto.org/en/press-release">{{cite web | url=http://www2.unwto.org/en/press-release/2012-11-05/international-tourism-strong-despite-uncertain-economy | title=International tourism strong despite uncertain economy | publisher=World Tourism Organization UNWTO | date=5 November 2012 | access-date=6 February 2013 | author=Press Release | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130218231404/http://www2.unwto.org/en/press-release/2012-11-05/international-tourism-strong-despite-uncertain-economy | archive-date=18 February 2013 | url-status=dead }}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://turystyka.rp.pl/trendy/nowe/24099-prezes-pit-bez-pomocy-panstwa-upadna-tysiace|title=Bez pomocy państwa upadną tysiące firm turystycznych|first=przez Filip Frydrykiewicz-9|last=marca 2020|date=9 March 2020}}</ref>

Tourist attractions in Poland vary, from the mountains in the south to the sandy beaches in the north, with a trail of nearly every architectural style. The most visited city is [[Kraków]], which was the former capital of Poland and serves as a relic of the [[Polish Golden Age]] and the [[Renaissance in Poland|Renaissance]]. Kraków also held [[Royal coronations in Poland|royal coronations]] of [[List of Polish monarchs|most Polish kings and monarchs]] at [[Wawel]], the nation's chief historical landmark. Among other notable sites in the country is [[Wrocław]], one of the oldest cities in Poland which was a model for the founding of Kraków. Wrocław is famous for its [[Wrocław's dwarfs|dwarf statues]], a large [[Market Square, Wrocław|market square]] with two [[Ratusz|town halls]], and the oldest [[Wrocław Zoo|Zoological Gardens]] with one of the world's largest number of animal [[species]]. The Polish capital [[Warsaw]] and its historical [[Warsaw Old Town|Old Town]] were entirely reconstructed after [[Destruction of Warsaw|wartime destruction]]. Other cities attracting countless tourists include [[Gdańsk]], [[Poznań]], [[Lublin]], [[Toruń]] as well as the site of the [[Germany|German]] [[Auschwitz concentration camp]] in [[Oświęcim]]. A notable highlight is the 13th-century [[Wieliczka Salt Mine]] with its labyrinthine tunnels, a [[Underground lake|subterranean lake]] and chapels carved by miners out of [[rock salt]] beneath the ground.
[[File:Afrykarium tunel.jpg|thumb|[[Africarium|Aquarium]] in the [[Wrocław Zoo|Zoological Garden]] in [[Wrocław]]]]
Poland's main tourist offerings include outdoor activities such as [[skiing]], [[sailing]], mountain [[hiking]] and [[climbing]], as well as [[agritourism]], sightseeing [[List of Historic Monuments (Poland)|historical monuments]]. Tourist destinations include the [[Baltic Sea]] coast in the north; the [[Masurian Lake District]] and [[Białowieża Forest]] in the east; on the south [[Karkonosze]], the [[Table Mountains]] and the [[Tatra Mountains]], where [[Rysy]] – the highest peak of Poland, and [[Orla Perć|Eagle's Path]] mountain trail are located. The [[Pieniny]] and [[Bieszczady Mountains]] lie in the extreme south-east.<ref name="turism" /> There are [[List of castles in Poland|over 100 castles]] in the country, most in the [[Lower Silesian Voivodeship]], and also on the [[Trail of the Eagles' Nests]].<ref>{{cite book |author1=Neil Wilson |author2=Tom Parkinson |author3=Richard Watkins |year=2005 |chapter-url=https://books.google.com/books?id=2LId4cLRMkoC&pg=PA164 |title=Poland |chapter=The Eagles' Nests |publisher=Lonely Planet |isbn=978-1-74059-522-3 |via=Google Books}}</ref> The largest castle in the world by land area is situated in [[Malbork Castle|Malbork]], in north-central Poland.<ref>{{Cite book|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=unN9DwAAQBAJ&q=malbork+castle+largest&pg=PT191|title=The 50 Greatest Castles and Palaces of the World|first=Gilly|last=Pickup|date=7 March 2019|publisher=Icon Books|isbn=978-1-78578-458-3|via=Google Books}}</ref>

=== Energy ===
{{Main|Energy in Poland|Coal mining in Poland}}
[[File:Bełchatów Elektrownia.jpg|thumb|left|[[Bełchatów Power Station]] is a [[lignite]]-fired [[Steam-electric power station|power station]] that produces 27–28 TWh of electricity per year or twenty per cent of the total power generation in Poland.]]

The electricity generation sector in Poland is largely [[Fossil fuel|fossil-fuel]]–based. Many power plants nationwide use Poland's position as a major European exporter of coal to their advantage by continuing to use coal as the primary raw material in the production of their energy. In 2013, Poland scored 48 out of 129 states in the Energy Sustainability Index.<ref name="Energy Sustainability Index" /> The three largest Polish coal mining firms ([[Węglokoks]], [[Kompania Węglowa]] and [[Jastrzębska Spółka Węglowa|JSW]]) extract around 100 million tonnes of coal annually.

[[Renewable energy|Renewable forms of energy]] account for a smaller proportion of Poland's full energy generation capacity.<ref name="EU Commission – Energy factsheet P74" /> However, the national government has set targets for the development of renewable energy sources in Poland (the share of energy from renewable sources in the gross final energy consumption in 2019 was – 12,18%). Increasing the share of energy from renewable sources and a significant reduction in [[Carbon dioxide in Earth's atmosphere|CO2 emissions]] to be achieved with the help of [[biofuel]]s, [[photovoltaics]], construction of [[wind farm]]s on the land and the [[Baltic Sea]], [[hydroelectric]] stations and [[nuclear power plant]].

Poland has around 164,800,000,000 m<sup>3</sup> of proven natural gas reserves and around 96,380,000 barrels of proven oil reserves. These reserves are exploited by energy supply companies such as [[PKN Orlen]] ("the only Polish company listed in the [[Fortune Global 500]]"), [[PGNiG]]. However, the small amounts of fossil fuels naturally occurring in Poland are insufficient to satisfy the full energy consumption needs of the population and industry.  Consequently, the country is a net importer of oil and natural gas. Therefore, since the second decade of the 21st century, Poland has been strongly developing the so-called North Gate in which the most important components are the [[Baltic Pipe]], the [[Świnoujście LNG terminal]] and Floating Storage and Regasification Unit in [[Port of Gdańsk]].

The five largest companies supplying Poland electricity are [[Polska Grupa Energetyczna|PGE]], [[Tauron Group|Tauron]], [[Enea SA|Enea]], [[:pl:Energa|Energa]] and [[Innogy|Innogy Poland]].

=== Transport ===
{{Main|Transport in Poland|List of airports in Poland|Highways in Poland}}
[[File:WK15 Wrocław Główny (2) Lichen99.jpg|thumb|left|[[Polish State Railways|PKP Intercity]] [[New Pendolino|Pendolino]] at the [[Wrocław Główny railway station|Wrocław railway station]]]]

Transport in Poland is provided by means of [[Rail transport in Poland|rail]], [[Roads and expressways in Poland|road]], [[Polish Merchant Navy|marine shipping]] and [[List of airports in Poland|air travel]]. The country is part of EU's [[Schengen Area]] and is an important transport hub along neighbouring [[Germany]] due to its strategic position in [[Central Europe]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.paih.gov.pl/poland_in_figures/transport|title=PAIH &#124; Transport|website=www.paih.gov.pl}}</ref> Some of the longest European routes, including the [[European route E40|E40]], run through Poland.

The country has a good network of [[Highways in Poland|highways]], composed of [[Limited-access road|express roads]] and [[Controlled-access highway|motorways]]. At the start of 2020, Poland had {{cvt|4146.5|km}} of highways in use.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.gddkia.gov.pl/pl/926/autostrady|title=Autostrady :: Generalna Dyrekcja Dróg Krajowych i Autostrad – Serwis informacyjny|website=www.gddkia.gov.pl}}</ref> In addition, all local and regional roads are monitored by the National Road Rebuilding Programme, which aims to improve the quality of travel in the countryside and suburban localities.<ref name="National Road Rebuilding Program (Polish)" />

In 2017, the nation had {{convert|18513|km}} of railway track, the third longest in Europe after [[Germany]] and [[France]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.statista.com/statistics/451500/length-of-railway-lines-in-use-in-europe/|title=Length of the rail network in Europe 2017, by country|website=Statista}}</ref> The [[Polish State Railways]] (PKP) is the dominant railway operator in the country. In December 2014, Poland began to implement [[High-speed rail in Poland|high–speed rail routes]] connecting major Polish cities,<ref name="dec23" /> and started passenger service using the [[New Pendolino]] train, operating at 200&nbsp;km/h on the [[PKP rail line 4|Central Rail Line]] (CMK). Polish regulations allow trains without [[European Train Control System|ETCS]] to travel at speeds up to 160&nbsp;km/h, trains with ETCS1 up to 200&nbsp;km/h, and trains with ETCS2 at over 200&nbsp;km/h. Most inter-regional connections rail routes in Poland are operated by [[PKP Intercity]], whilst regional trains are run by a number of private operators, the largest of which is [[Polregio]]. The largest passenger [[train station]] in terms of the number of travelers is [[Wrocław Główny railway station|Wrocław Główny]].

[[File:LOT Polish Airlines Boing 787-8 SP-LRD NRT (24747512573).jpg|thumb|right|[[LOT Polish Airlines]] is Poland's [[flag carrier]], originally established in 1928.]]

The air and maritime transport markets in Poland are largely well developed. Poland has a number of international airports, the largest of which is [[Warsaw Chopin Airport]], the primary global hub for [[LOT Polish Airlines]]. It was established in 1928 from a merger of [[Aerolloyd]] (1922) and [[Aero (Polish airline)|Aero]] (1925). Other major airports with international connections include [[John Paul II International Airport Kraków–Balice]], [[Copernicus Airport Wrocław]], [[Gdańsk Lech Wałęsa Airport]]. Poland has begun preparations for a construction that can handle 100 million passengers of the [[New Central Polish Airport|Central Communication Port]].

Seaports exist all along Poland's Baltic coast, with most freight operations using [[Port of Świnoujście|Świnoujście]], [[Port of Police|Police]], [[Port of Szczecin|Szczecin]], [[Port of Kołobrzeg|Kołobrzeg]], [[Port of Gdynia|Gdynia]], [[Port of Gdańsk|Gdańsk]] and [[Elbląg]] as their base.
Passenger ferries link Poland with [[Scandinavia]] all year round; these services are provided from Gdańsk and Świnoujście by [[Polferries]], [[Stena Line]] from Gdynia and [[Unity Line]] from the Świnoujście. The [[Port of Gdańsk]] is the only port in the [[Baltic Sea]] adapted to receive oceanic vessels.

=== Science and technology ===
{{Main|Polish science and technology|Poles#Science and technology}}
[[File:Marie Curie c1920.png|thumb|upright=0.7|left|Physicist and chemist [[Marie Curie|Maria Skłodowska-Curie]] was the first person to win two [[Nobel Prize]]s. She also established Poland's [[Curie Institute (Warsaw)|Radium Institute]] in 1925.<ref name="A century of X-rays and radioactivity in medicine: with emphasis on photographic records of the early years" />]]

Over the course of history, the Polish people have made considerable contributions in the fields of science, technology and mathematics.<ref>{{Cite book|url=http://uatacz.up.krakow.pl/~wwwchemia/pliki/ISBN_978_83_7271_768_9_From_alchemy_to_the_present_day|title=From alchemy to the present day – the choice of biographies of Polish scientists|last1=Nodzyńska|first1=Małgorzata|last2=Cieśla|first2=Paweł|publisher=Pedagogical University of Kraków|year=2012|isbn=978-83-7271-768-9|location=Cracow}}</ref> Perhaps the most renowned Pole to support this theory was [[Nicolaus Copernicus]] (''Mikołaj Kopernik''), who triggered the [[Copernican Revolution]] by placing the [[Heliocentrism|Sun rather than the Earth at the center of the universe]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.space.com/15684-nicolaus-copernicus.html|title=Nicolaus Copernicus Biography: Facts & Discoveries|website=[[Space.com]]|date=20 March 2018|access-date=6 April 2018}}</ref> He also derived a [[quantity theory of money]], which made him a pioneer of economics. Copernicus' achievements and discoveries are considered the basis of Polish culture and cultural identity.<ref>{{Cite book|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=_RZcA9o8IVAC&q=copernicus+polish+identity+and+culture&pg=PA163|title=Forced Out: The Fate of Polish Jewry in Communist Poland|first=Arthur J.|last=Wolak|date=12 March 2004|publisher=Arthur Wolak|isbn=978-1-58736-291-0|via=Google Books}}</ref>

Poland's tertiary education institutions; traditional [[List of universities in Poland|universities]], as well as technical, medical, and economic institutions, employ around tens of thousands of researchers and staff members. There are hundreds of research and development institutes.<ref>{{Cite journal|url=https://content.sciendo.com/view/journals/minib/21/3/article-p141.xml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200501152808/https://content.sciendo.com/view/journals/minib/21/3/article-p141.xml|url-status=dead|archive-date=1 May 2020|title=Research Institutes In Poland — Evaluation of Their Place and Role in Innovative Politics in Poland|first=Renata|last=Barcikowska|date=1 September 2016|journal=Marketing of Scientific and Research Organizations|volume=21|issue=3|pages=141–154|via=content.sciendo.com|doi=10.14611/minib.21.09.2016.12|s2cid=199470591}}</ref> However, in the 19th and 20th centuries many Polish scientists worked abroad; one of the most important of these exiles was [[Maria Skłodowska-Curie]], a physicist and chemist who lived much of her life in France. In 1925 she established Poland's [[Curie Institute (Warsaw)|Radium Institute]].<ref name="A century of X-rays and radioactivity in medicine: with emphasis on photographic records of the early years" />

[[File:Nikolaus Kopernikus.jpg|thumb|right|upright|[[Nicolaus Copernicus]], the 16th century Polish astronomer who formulated the [[Heliocentrism|heliocentric]] model of the solar system that placed the Sun rather than the Earth at its center.]]

In the first half of the 20th century, Poland was a flourishing centre of mathematics. Outstanding Polish mathematicians formed the [[Lwów School of Mathematics]] (with [[Stefan Banach]], [[Stanisław Mazur]], [[Hugo Steinhaus]], [[Stanisław Ulam]]) and [[Warsaw School of Mathematics]] (with [[Alfred Tarski]], [[Kazimierz Kuratowski]], [[Wacław Sierpiński]] and [[Antoni Zygmund]]). Numerous mathematicians, scientists, chemists or economists emigrated due to historic vicissitudes, among them [[Benoit Mandelbrot]], [[Leonid Hurwicz]], [[Alfred Tarski]], [[Joseph Rotblat]] and [[Nobel Prize]] laureates [[Roald Hoffmann]], [[Georges Charpak]] and [[Tadeusz Reichstein]]. In the 1930s, mathematician and cryptologist [[Marian Rejewski]] invented the [[Bomba (cryptography)|Cryptographic Bomb]] which formed the basis of the effort that allowed the Allies to crack the [[Enigma code]].

Over 40 research and development centers and 4,500 researchers make Poland the biggest research and development hub in Central and Eastern Europe.<ref name="autogenerated2" /><ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.chicagotribune.com/news/sns-rt-us-poland-immigrantstre7bs11w-20111229,0,2982543.story |title=Topic Galleries |work=chicagotribune.com |access-date=6 February 2012}}{{dead link|date=March 2017|bot=medic}}{{cbignore|bot=medic}}</ref> Multinational companies such as: ABB, [[Delphi Corporation|Delphi]], [[GlaxoSmithKline]], [[Google]], [[Hewlett–Packard]], [[IBM]], [[Intel]], [[LG Electronics]], [[Microsoft]], [[Motorola]], [[Siemens]] and [[Samsung]] all have set up research and development centres in Poland.<ref name="autogenerated1" /> Companies chose Poland because of the availability of highly qualified labour force, presence of universities, support of authorities, and the largest market in East-Central Europe.<ref name="autogenerated2" /> According to a [[KPMG]] report from 2011, 80% of Poland's current investors are content with their choice and willing to reinvest.<ref name="Why Poland?" /> Poland was ranked 38th in the [[Global Innovation Index]] in 2020, up from 39th in 2019.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Release of the Global Innovation Index 2020: Who Will Finance Innovation?|url=https://www.wipo.int/global_innovation_index/en/2020/index.html|access-date=2021-09-02|website=www.wipo.int|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|title=Global Innovation Index 2019|url=https://www.wipo.int/global_innovation_index/en/2019/index.html|access-date=2021-09-02|website=www.wipo.int|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|title=RTD - Item|url=https://ec.europa.eu/newsroom/rtd/items/691898|access-date=2021-09-02|website=ec.europa.eu}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|date=2013-10-28|title=Global Innovation Index|url=https://knowledge.insead.edu/entrepreneurship-innovation/global-innovation-index-2930|access-date=2021-09-02|website=INSEAD Knowledge|language=en}}</ref>

Poland has a very well-developed e-administration, thanks to which many official matters can be easily and quickly settled via the Internet. In the UN ranking, Poland is in the top twenty countries with the best-rated e-administration in the world.

== Demographics ==
{{Main|Demographics of Poland|List of cities and towns in Poland|Metropolitan areas in Poland|Polish diaspora}}
{{Largest cities of Poland}}{{Clear}}

Poland, with approximately 38.5 million inhabitants, has the [[List of European countries by population|ninth-largest population in Europe]] and the fifth-largest in the [[European Union]]. It has a population density of 122 inhabitants per square kilometre (328 per square mile). The [[total fertility rate]] in 2020 was estimated at 1.44 children born to a woman, a considerable rise from previous years.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.macrotrends.net/countries/POL/poland/fertility-rate|title=Poland Fertility Rate 1950–2020|website=www.macrotrends.net}}</ref> In contrast, the total fertility rate in 1925 was 4.68.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.statista.com/statistics/1033939/fertility-rate-poland-1800-2020/|title=Poland: fertility rate 1800–2020|website=Statista}}</ref> Furthermore, Poland's population is aging significantly and the median age in 2018 was 41.1 years.<ref name="auto1">{{Cite web|url=https://www.indexmundi.com/poland/demographics_profile.html|title=Poland Demographics Profile 2019|website=www.indexmundi.com}}</ref> The crude death rate in 2020 stood at 10.3 per 1,000 people.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.macrotrends.net/countries/POL/poland/death-rate|title=Poland Death Rate 1950–2020|website=www.macrotrends.net}}</ref>

[[File:Population of Poland.svg|upright=1.1|thumb|Population of Poland from 1900 to 2010 in millions of inhabitants]]

Around 60% of [[Poles]] and Polish citizens reside in urban areas or major cities and 40% in more rural zones.<ref name="auto1"/> The most populous administrative province or state is the [[Masovian Voivodeship]] and the most populous city is the capital, [[Warsaw]], at 1.8 million inhabitants with a further 2-3 million people living in its [[Warsaw metropolitan area|metropolitan area]].<ref>[http://www.mrr.gov.pl/polityka_regionalna/SRPW_2020/Dokumenty%20i%20ekspertyzy/Documents/17d0ccd2c3f14ed3893369e56d59849cMarkowski.pdf Funkcje Metropolitalne Pięciu Stolic Województw Wschodnich] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090327120341/http://www.mrr.gov.pl/polityka_regionalna/SRPW_2020/Dokumenty%20i%20ekspertyzy/Documents/17d0ccd2c3f14ed3893369e56d59849cMarkowski.pdf |date=2009-03-27 }} - [[:pl:Tadeusz Markowski (ekonomista)|Markowski]]</ref><ref>[https://www.un.org/esa/population/publications/wup2003/2003WUPHighlights.pdf ''World Urbanization Prospects''] - [[United Nations]] - Department of Economic and Social Affairs / Population Division, The 2003 Revision (data of 2000)</ref><ref>[[Eurostat]], [http://www.urbanaudit.org/DataAccessed.aspx Urban Audit database] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110406130058/http://www.urbanaudit.org/DataAccessed.aspx |date=2011-04-06 }}, accessed on 2009-03-12. Data for 2004.</ref> The [[Katowice urban area|metropolitan area]] of [[Katowice]] is the largest urban [[conurbation]] in Poland with a population between 2.7 million<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.newgeography.com/content/003879-major-metropolitan-areas-europe |title=Major Metropolitan Areas in Europe |last=Cox |first=Wendell |date=2013 |website=New Geography |publisher=Joel Kotkin and Praxis Strategy Group}}</ref> and 5.3 million residents.<ref>[[European Spatial Planning Observation Network]], [https://www.espon.eu/sites/default/files/attachments/fr-1.4.3_April2007-final.pdf Study on Urban Functions (Project 1.4.3)] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150924002318/http://www.espon.eu/export/sites/default/Documents/Projects/ESPON2006Projects/StudiesScientificSupportProjects/UrbanFunctions/fr-1.4.3_April2007-final.pdf |date=2015-09-24 }}, Final Report, Chapter 3, (ESPON, 2007)</ref> The least populous and the smallest province in size is the [[Opole Voivodeship]], with just under 1 million people living within its borders. Hence, a substantial portion of the total population is concentrated in the south of Poland, roughly between the cities of [[Wrocław]] and [[Kraków]].

In the [[Polish census of 2011|2011 Polish census]], 37,310,341 people reported [[Poles|Polish]] identity, 846,719 [[Silesians|Silesian]], 232,547 [[Kashubians|Kashubian]] and 147,814 [[German minority in Poland|German]]. Other [[Poles#National minorities|identities]] were reported by 163,363 people (0.41%) and 521,470 people (1.35%) did not specify any nationality.<ref name="GUS97" /><ref name="GUS98" /> Once prominent but now statistically insignificant minority groups include [[History of the Jews in Poland|Polish Jews]], [[Lipka Tatars]], [[Armenians in Poland|Armenians]], [[Greeks in Poland|Greeks]], [[Lemkos]], the [[Romani people in Poland|Romani people]] and the [[Vietnamese in Poland|Vietnamese]]. Ethnic Poles themselves can be divided into many diverse [[Regions of Poland|regional]] [[Ethnography|ethnographic]] sub-groups, most notable being the [[Kashubians]], [[Silesians]] and [[Gorals]] (Highlanders). The statistics do not include recently arrived migrant workers.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Santora |first1=Marc |title=Poland Bashes Immigrants, but Quietly Takes Christian Ones |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/03/26/world/europe/immigration-poland-ukraine-christian.html |work=The New York Times |date=26 March 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Walker |first1=Shaun |title='A whole generation has gone': Ukrainians seek a better life in Poland |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2019/apr/18/whole-generation-has-gone-ukrainian-seek-better-life-poland-elect-president |work=The Guardian |date=18 April 2019}}</ref> More than 1.7 million Ukrainian citizens worked legally in Poland in 2017.<ref>{{cite news |title=Filling Poland's labour gap |url=https://poland-today.pl/filling-polands-labour-gap/ |access-date=24 March 2019 |work=Poland Today}}</ref>

There is a very strong [[Polish diaspora]] around the world, notably in the [[Polish Americans|United States]], [[Poles in Germany|Germany]], [[Poles in the United Kingdom|United Kingdom]] and [[Polish Canadians|Canada]].<ref name="Centers of Polish Immigration in the World – USA and Germany" /> A strong Polish minority is still present in the territories of contemporary western Ukraine and Belarus, eastern Lithuania, eastern and central Latvia, and northeastern Czech Republic, which were part of Poland in the past. Altogether, the number of ethnic Poles living abroad is estimated to be around 20&nbsp;million.<ref name="Polish Diaspora (Polonia) Worldwide" />

=== Languages ===
{{Main|Polish language|Languages of Poland|Bilingual communes in Poland}}
[[File:Dolina Jadwigi znak.jpg|thumb|upright=1.1|''Dolina Jadwigi'' — a [[bilingual]] Polish-[[Kashubian language|Kashubian]] road sign with the village name]]

[[Polish language|Polish]] is the only [[official language|official]] and predominant spoken language in Poland, but it is also used throughout the world by [[Polish diaspora|Polish minorities]] in other countries as well as being one of the official [[languages of the European Union]]. The deaf communities use [[Polish Sign Language]] belonging to the [[German Sign Language|German family of Sign Languages]]. Polish is also a [[second language]] in parts of [[Lithuania]], where it is taught in Polish-minority schools.<ref>{{cite act|url=http://conventions.coe.int/Treaty/Commun/QueVoulezVous.asp?NT=157&CM=2&DF=18/04/02&CL=ENG|title=Framework Convention for the Protection of National Minorities|index=157|type=Treaty|legislature=Council of Europe|date=1 February 1995|access-date=15 September 2021}}</ref><ref>{{Cite book|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=LQ92DwAAQBAJ&q=polish+taught+in+schools+in+lithuania&pg=PA164|title=Multilingualism in the Baltic States: Societal Discourses and Contact Phenomena|first1=Sanita|last1=Lazdiņa|first2=Heiko F.|last2=Marten|date=3 November 2018|publisher=Springer|isbn=978-1-137-56914-1|via=Google Books}}</ref> Contemporary Poland is a linguistically [[homogeneous]] nation, with nearly 97% of respondents declaring Polish as their mother tongue.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.worldatlas.com/articles/what-languages-are-spoken-in-poland.html|title=Which Languages Are Spoken in Poland?|website=WorldAtlas|date=18 July 2018}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.diskusija.lt/languages/languages-we-translate/polish-translation/#:~:text=Polish%20Language%20Facts&text=There%20are%20approximately%2040%20million,Lithuania%2C%20Belarus%2C%20and%20Ukraine.|title=Polish Translation Services &#124; Polish translator &#124; Diskusija}}</ref>
  
Poland's once multi-ethnic population communicated in numerous languages and [[lect]]s which faded or disappeared along the course of history. There are currently 15<ref>{{cite web |url=http://ksng.gugik.gov.pl/english/files/act_on_national_minorities.pdf |title=Act of 6 January 2005 on national and ethnic minorities and on the regional languages |via=GUGiK.gov.pl}}</ref> minority languages in Poland, including one recognized regional language, [[Kashubian language|Kashubian]], which is spoken by around 366,000 people in the northern regions of [[Kashubia]] and [[Pomerania]].<ref>{{Cite journal|date=September 2011|title=Polen-Analysen. Die Kaschuben|url=http://www.laender-analysen.de/polen/pdf/PolenAnalysen95.pdf|journal=Länder-Analysen|language=de|volume=Polen NR. 95|pages=10–13}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=http://docplayer.pl/57273906-Instytut-kaszubski-acta-cassubiana-tom-xvii.html|title=Acta Cassubiana. Vol. XVII (map on p. 122)|date=2015|website=Instytut Kaszubski|access-date=9 February 2018}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://instytutkaszubski.republika.pl/pdfy/niemiecki.pdf|title=Kaschuben heute: Kultur-Sprache-Identität|date=2007|language=de|access-date=3 January 2016|archive-date=3 January 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160103000918/http://instytutkaszubski.republika.pl/pdfy/niemiecki.pdf|url-status=dead}}</ref>

Languages having a minority status are Armenian, Belarusian, Czech, German, Yiddish, Hebrew, Lithuanian, Russian, Slovak and Ukrainian. Languages having the status of ethnic minority's language are [[Karaim language|Karaim]], [[Rusyn language|Lemko-Rusyn]], [[Tatar language|Tatar]] and two [[Romani languages]]; [[Polska Roma]] and [[Bergitka Roma]].<ref>According to [[Ethnologue]] the following Romani languages are spoken in Poland: [[Vlax Romani language|Romani Vlax]], [[North Central Romani|Romani Carpathian]], [[Sinte Romani|Romani Sinte]], [[Romani language|Baltic Romani]]. See: [http://www.ethnologue.com/show_country.asp?name=PL ''Ethnologue. Languages of the World'', Ethnologue report for Poland] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130104034421/http://www.ethnologue.com/show_country.asp?name=PL |date=4 January 2013}}</ref> Official recognition of a language provides certain rights under conditions prescribed by Polish law, including education and state financial support for promoting that language. Poland recognized [[Bilingual communes in Poland|secondary administrative languages or auxiliary languages in bilingual municipalities]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://isap.sejm.gov.pl/isap.nsf/DocDetails.xsp?id=WDU20170000823|title=Obwieszczenie Marszałka Sejmu Rzeczypospolitej Polskiej z dnia 5 kwietnia 2017 r. w sprawie ogłoszenia jednolitego tekstu ustawy o mniejszościach narodowych i etnicznych oraz o języku regionalnym|website=isap.sejm.gov.pl}}</ref> Currently, German and Kashubian hold such status in 19 municipalities (''[[gmina]]s''), Belarusian in 9 and Lithuanian in 1. Bilingual signs, names and advertisements are commonplace in those localities. [[Silesian language|Silesian]] and [[Wymysorys language|Wymysorys]] (Vilamovian) are not legally recognized or acknowledged as separate languages with a minority status.

More than 50% of Polish citizens declare at least basic knowledge of the [[English language]], followed by [[German language|German]] (38%).<ref>{{cite web|url=http://wiadomosci.onet.pl/swiat/tns-polska-ponad-polowa-polakow-zna-jezyk-angielski/xm49ll |title=TNS Polska: ponad połowa Polaków zna język angielski |trans-title=TNS Poland: more than half of Poles know English |language=pl |publisher=onet.pl |date=17 June 2015 |access-date=10 February 2016}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=http://serwisy.gazetaprawna.pl/edukacja/artykuly/1111366,jakie-jezyki-obce-znaja-polacy.html|title=Jakie języki obce znają Polacy?|website=serwisy.gazetaprawna.pl|date=15 March 2018}}</ref>

=== Religion ===
{{bar box
|title=Religions in Poland (2015)
|titlebar=#ddd
|float=right
|bars=
{{bar percent|Roman Catholic|SteelBlue|92.9}}
{{bar percent|Irreligion|red|3.1}}
{{bar percent|No answer|gold|2.7}}
{{bar percent|Other faiths|MediumAquaMarine|1.3}}
|caption=Numbers from the Central Statistical Office:<ref name="GUS2016">{{Cite web|url=https://stat.gov.pl/en/infographics-and-widgets/infographics/infographic-religiousness-of-polish-inhabitiants,4,1.html|title=Infographic – Religiousness of Polish inhabitiants|last=GUS|website=stat.gov.pl|language=en|access-date=17 June 2019}}</ref>
}}
{{Main|Religion in Poland}}

According to the 2015 census, 92.9% of all Polish citizens adhere to the [[Roman Catholic Church in Poland|Roman Catholic Church]]. An estimated 94.2% of the population are believers and 3.1% are [[Atheism|irreligious]], making Poland one of the more devout countries in Europe.<ref name="auto2">{{Cite web|url=https://stat.gov.pl/en/infographics-and-widgets/infographics/infographic-religiousness-of-polish-inhabitiants,4,1.html|title=Infographic – Religiousness of Polish inhabitiants|website=stat.gov.pl}}</ref> Around 61.6% of all respondents outlined that religion is of high or very high importance.<ref name="auto2"/> However, church attendance has decreased in recent years; only 38% of worshippers attended [[Mass (liturgy)|mass]] regularly on Sunday in 2018.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://wpolityce.pl/kosciol/480915-ilu-polakow-uczestniczy-we-mszy-sw-sprawdz-statystyki-iskk|title=Ilu Polaków uczestniczy we Mszy św.? SPRAWDŹ statystyki ISKK|website=wpolityce.pl}}</ref> Freedom of religion is guaranteed by the Polish Constitution,<ref name="Wyznania religijne" /><ref name="www10" /> and the [[concordat]] guarantees the teaching of religion in state schools.<ref>{{cite web | url=http://isap.sejm.gov.pl/Download?id=WDU19980510318&type=2 | title=Konkordat | publisher=Sejm | date=28 July 1993 | access-date=28 June 2014}}</ref>

[[File:Odnowa w Duchu Świętym - Jasna Góra 2011.jpg|thumb|left|[[Jasna Góra Monastery]] in [[Częstochowa]] is a shrine to the [[Black Madonna of Częstochowa]], and a major pilgrimage site for Poland's many Catholics.]]

For centuries the tribes inhabiting the lands of modern-day Poland have practised various forms of [[paganism]] known as ''[[Slavic Native Faith|Rodzimowierstwo]]'', or "native faith".<ref>Gniazdo – Rodzima wiara i kultura, nr 2(7)/2009 – Ratomir Wilkowski: Rozważania o wizerunku rodzimowierstwa na przykładzie...</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://rkp.org.pl/|title=Rodzimy Kościół Polski|first=Keios|last=Solutions|website=Rodzimy Kościół Polski|access-date=27 March 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://wildhunt.org/2016/07/paganism-in-poland.html|title=Paganism in Poland|date=6 July 2016|website=The Wild Hunt|access-date=27 March 2019}}</ref> In the year 966, Duke [[Mieszko I]] converted to [[Christianity]], and submitted to the authority of the [[Roman Catholic Church]].<ref>{{cite book|author=Norman Davies|title=God's Playground: The origins to 1795|url=https://archive.org/details/godsplaygroundhi00norm_0|url-access=registration|access-date=5 April 2012|date=30 March 2005|publisher=Columbia University Press|isbn=978-0-231-12817-9|page=[https://archive.org/details/godsplaygroundhi00norm_0/page/57 57]}}</ref><ref>{{cite book|author=Halina Lerski|title=Historical Dictionary of Poland, 966–1945|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=luRry4Y5NIYC&pg=PA27|access-date=5 April 2012|date=30 January 1996|publisher=ABC-CLIO|isbn=978-0-313-03456-5|page=27}}</ref> This event came to be known as the [[Christianization of Poland|Baptism of Poland]].<ref>Juliusz Bardach, Boguslaw Lesnodorski, and Michal Pietrzak, ''Historia panstwa i prawa polskiego'' Warsaw: Paristwowe Wydawnictwo Naukowe, 1987, pp.53–54</ref><ref>''Chrystianizacja Polski południowej.'' Materiały sesji naukowej odbytej 29 czerwca 1993 roku, Kraków, 1994</ref><ref>{{cite book|author=Norman Davies|title=God's Playground: The origins to 1795|url=https://archive.org/details/godsplaygroundhi00norm_0|url-access=registration|access-date=5 April 2012|date=30 March 2005|publisher=Columbia University Press|isbn=978-0-231-12817-9|pages=[https://archive.org/details/godsplaygroundhi00norm_0/page/15 15]–17}}</ref> However, this did not put an end to pagan beliefs in the country. The persistence was demonstrated by a series of rebellions in the 1030s known as the [[Pagan reaction in Poland|pagan reaction]], which also showed elements of a peasant uprising against medieval [[feudalism]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.krakowpost.com/6956/2013/08/resurgence-of-pre-christian-beliefs-in-poland|title=Resurgence of Pre-Christian Beliefs in Poland|first=Grażyna|last=Zawada|date=29 August 2013|access-date=27 March 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite book|author=Polska Akademia Nauk. Komitet Słowianoznawstwa|title=Słownik starożytności słowiańskich: encyklopedyczny zarys kultury słowian od czasów najdawniejszych|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=KQ_vAAAAMAAJ|access-date=27 March 2013|year=1967|publisher=Zkład Narodowy im. Ossolińskich|page=247|quote=Widziano w M. wodza powstania pogańsko-ludowego}}</ref>

[[File:Pope John Paul II (18731175945).jpg|thumb|right|upright|[[Karol Wojtyła]] was the first [[Poles|Pole]] to become a [[Catholic Church|Roman Catholic]] Pope ([[John Paul II]]). He held the papacy between 1978 and 2005.]]

Religious tolerance was an important part of Polish political culture, though it [[Edict of Wieluń|varied]] at times. In 1264, the [[Statute of Kalisz]] granted [[Jews]] unprecedented legal rights not found anywhere in Europe. In 1573, the [[Warsaw Confederation]] marked the formal beginning of extensive religious freedoms in Poland. It was partially influenced by the 1572 [[St. Bartholomew's Day Massacre]] in [[France]], which prompted the nobility to prevent the monarch from carrying out reprehensible atrocities in Poland based on religious affiliation.<ref>Adam Zamojski, "The Polish Way". New York: Hippocrene Books, 1987</ref> The religious tolerance also spurred many theological movements such as the Calvinist [[Polish Brethren]], a number of Protestant groups and [[Atheism|atheists]] like [[Kazimierz Łyszczyński|Casimir Liszinski]], one of the first atheist thinkers in Europe.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.michaelnugent.com/2020/01/06/casimir-liszinski/|title=Casimir Liszinski, executed for atheism – Michael Nugent}}</ref> [[Anabaptist]]s fleeing 16th-century persecution in the [[Netherlands]] and Germany settled in Poland and became known as the [[Vistula delta Mennonites]]. From 16 October 1978 until his death on 2 April 2005, Cardinal [[John Paul II|Karol Józef Wojtyła]] was head of the Roman Catholic Church as [[Pope]] John Paul II.<ref name="About" /><ref name="Domínguez" /><ref name="Communism" />

Contemporary religious minorities include [[Polish Orthodox Church|Christian Orthodox]] (506,800),<ref name="CSO_2008" /> various [[Protestants]] (150,000) — including 77,500 [[Lutherans]] of the [[Evangelical-Augsburg Church in Poland|Evangelical-Augsburg Church]],<ref name="CSO_2008" /> 23,000 [[Pentecostalism|Pentecostals]] in the [[Pentecostal Church in Poland]], 10,000 [[Adventists]] in the [[Seventh-day Adventist Church]] and other smaller [[Evangelicalism|Evangelical]] denominations<ref name="CSO_2008" /> — [[Jehovah's Witnesses]] (126,827),<ref name="CSO_2008" /> [[Eastern Catholic Churches|Eastern Catholics]], [[Mariavite Church|Mariavites]], [[History of the Jews in Poland|Jews]], [[Islam in Poland|Muslims]] ([[Tatars]]) and [[Modern Paganism|neopagans]], some of whom are members of the [[Native Polish Church]].

[[File:Inside old synagogue Krakow.JPG|thumb|left|The [[Old Synagogue, Kraków|Old Synagogue]] of [[Kraków]] is the oldest standing synagogue in Poland. [[Hasidic Judaism]] originated in the [[Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth]] during the 18th century.]]

Famous sites of Roman Catholic pilgrimage in Poland include the [[Jasna Góra Monastery|Monastery of Jasna Góra]] in the city of [[Częstochowa]], [[Basilica of Our Lady of Licheń]], Kraków's [[Divine Mercy Sanctuary, Kraków|Sanctuary of Divine Mercy]] and [[Święta Lipka Sanctuary|Święta Lipka]] (Holy Linden) in [[Masuria]]. Tourists also visit the [[Holy Father John Paul II Family Home in Wadowice|family home of John Paul II]] in [[Wadowice]] outside [[Kraków]]. [[Christ the King (Świebodzin)|Christ the King]] in [[Świebodzin]] is the [[List of statues by height|one of the tallest]] statues of Jesus in the world.<ref>{{cite news |title=Giant Jesus Statue In Poland Now Distributing WiFi To Local Parish |url=http://yupthatexists.com/giant-jesus-statue-in-poland-now-distributing-wifi-to-local-parish/ |work=Yup That Exists |date=4 June 2019 |access-date=28 June 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190629042925/http://yupthatexists.com/giant-jesus-statue-in-poland-now-distributing-wifi-to-local-parish/ |archive-date=29 June 2019 |url-status=dead}}</ref> Christian Orthodox pilgrims visit Mount Grabarka near [[Grabarka-Klasztor]] and the [[Hasidic Jews]] travel annually to the grave of a great [[Elimelech of Lizhensk|rabbi]] in [[Leżajsk]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://mapa.nocowanie.pl/ossolin/zdjecia/25927277|title=Zdjęcie Ossolin – zdjęcia, fotografia Ossolin|access-date=1 January 2017}}</ref>

=== Health ===
{{Main|Health in Poland}}
Medical service providers and [[hospitals]] (''szpitale'') in Poland are subordinate to the [[Ministry of Health of the Republic of Poland|Ministry of Health]]; it provides administrative oversight and scrutiny of general medical practice, and is obliged to maintain a high standard of [[hygiene]] and patient care. Poland has a [[Universal health care|universal healthcare system]] based on an all-inclusive [[Health insurance|insurance system]]; state subsidised healthcare is available to all citizens covered by the general health insurance program of the [[National Health Fund]] (NFZ). Private medical complexes exist nationwide; over 50% of the population uses both public and private sectors.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.termedia.pl/mz/Niecierpliwi,34562.html|title=Niecierpliwi|website=www.termedia.pl}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.money.pl/gospodarka/wiadomosci/artykul/prywatnie-leczy-sie-juz-ponad-polowa-polakow,218,0,2416090.html#:~:text=Z%20danych%20Polskiej%20Izby%20Ubezpiecze%C5%84%20wynika%2C%20%C5%BCe%20ponad%20po%C5%82owa%20Polak%C3%B3w,Tylko%2038%20proc.|title = Prywatnie leczy się już ponad połowa Polaków}}</ref><ref name="justlanded" />

Hospitals are organised according to the regional administrative structure, resultantly most towns, [[Powiat|counties]] or [[Gmina|municipalities]] possess their own provincial hospital or medical [[clinic]]s.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://pranav-poland.blogspot.com.au/2010/12/health.html|title=POLAND: Health|last=Pranav|date=25 December 2010|access-date=24 April 2017}}</ref> There are six types of hospital facilities, each with a particular area of medical expertise – I Grade Hospitals for [[general surgery]], internal illnesses and [[obstetrics]]; II Grade Hospitals for child surgery, [[neurology]], cardiology and [[ophthalmology]]; III Grade Hospitals including [[teaching hospitals]] for infectious diseases, [[nephrology]], orthopedics, toxicology and transplantology; Oncology Hospitals for cancer treatment and [[brachytherapy]]; Pediatric Hospitals for child care; and Nationwide Hospitals for general and [[acute care]].<ref>http://isap.sejm.gov.pl/isap.nsf/download.xsp/WDU20170000844/O/D20170844.pdf</ref>

According to the [[HDI|Human Development Report]] from 2020, the average life expectancy at birth is 79 years (around 75 years for an infant male and 83 years for an infant female);<ref>{{cite web |url=http://hdr.undp.org/en/countries/profiles/POL |title=Poland – Human Development Indicators |date=2020 |website=Human Development Reports |publisher=United Nations Development Programme |access-date=16 December 2020}}</ref> the country has a low [[infant mortality rate]] (4 per 1,000 births).<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://data.worldbank.org/indicator/SP.DYN.IMRT.IN|title=Mortality rate, infant (per 1,000 live births) &#124; Data|website=data.worldbank.org}}</ref> In 2019, the principal cause of death was [[ischemic heart disease]]; diseases of the [[circulatory system]] accounted for 45% of all deaths.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://read.oecd-ilibrary.org/social-issues-migration-health/poland-country-health-profile-2019_297e4b92-en|title=Poland: Country Health Profile 2019 &#124; READ online|website=OECD iLibrary}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.compensa.pl/blog/78/prywatna-opieka-medyczna-czy-warto|title=Prywatna opieka medyczna – czy warto? – Blog – Compensa|website=www.compensa.pl}}</ref> In the same year, Poland was also the 15th-largest importer of [[medications]] and pharmaceutical products.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.worldstopexports.com/international-markets-for-imported-drugs-by-country/|title=Imports of Drugs and Medicines by Country|date=4 April 2020|website=World's Top Exports}}</ref>

=== Education ===
{{Main|Education in Poland|Universities in Poland}}
[[File:Jagiellonian University 05.jpg|thumb|300px|[[Jagiellonian University]] in [[Kraków]]]]

The [[Jagiellonian University]] founded in 1364 by [[Casimir III the Great|Casimir III]] in [[Kraków]] was the first institution of higher learning established in Poland, and is one of the [[List of oldest universities in continuous operation|oldest universities]] still in continuous operation.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://en.uj.edu.pl/en_GB/about-university/history|title=History – Jagiellonian University – Jagiellonian University|website=en.uj.edu.pl}}</ref> Poland's [[Commission of National Education]] (''Komisja Edukacji Narodowej''), established in 1773, was the world's first state ministry of education.<ref>{{cite book|author=Jan IJ. van der Meer|title=Literary Activities and Attitudes in the Stanislavian Age in Poland (1764–1795): A Social System?|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=-98Z_F7SWroC&pg=PA233|access-date=26 April 2012|year=2002|publisher=Rodopi|isbn=978-90-420-0933-2|page=233}}</ref><ref>{{cite book|author=Norman Davies|author-link=Norman Davies|title=God's Playground: 1795 to the present|url=https://archive.org/details/godsplaygroundhi00norm_0|url-access=registration|year=2005|publisher=Columbia University Press|isbn=978-0-231-12819-3|oclc=660185612|page=[https://archive.org/details/godsplaygroundhi00norm_0/page/167 167]}}</ref> 
 
The framework for [[primary education|primary]] and [[secondary education|secondary schooling]] in contemporary Poland is established by the [[Ministry of National Education (Poland)|Ministry of National Education]]. Kindergarten attendance is optional for children aged between three and five, with one year being [[compulsory education|compulsory]] for six-year-olds.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.dlaprzedszkolaka.info/s/4146/77362-Informacje/4080018-Zmiany-w-wychowaniu-przedszkolnym.htm|title=Zmiany w wychowaniu przedszkolnym - Informacje - Wychowanie przedszkolne w Polsce - wiek, obowiązek, miejsce, opłaty - dlaprzedszkolaka.info|website=www.dlaprzedszkolaka.info}}</ref><ref name="auto4">http://isap.sejm.gov.pl/isap.nsf/download.xsp/WDU20170000059/T/D20170059L.pdf</ref> Primary education traditionally begins at the age of seven, although children aged six can attend at the request of their parents or guardians.<ref name="auto4"/> Elementary school spans eight grades, at the end of which an obligatory three-part exam on Polish, mathematics and a foreign language is to be undertaken.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://cke.gov.pl/egzamin-osmoklasisty/o-egzaminie/|title=O egzaminie – CKE}}</ref> Secondary schooling is dependent on student preference – either a four-year high school (''[[General education liceum|liceum]]''), a five-year technical school (''[[Technikum (Polish education)|technikum]]'') or various [[vocational school|vocational studies]] (''szkoła branżowa'') can be pursued by each individual pupil.<ref name="auto4"/> A liceum or technikum is concluded with a maturity exit exam (''[[matura]]''), which must be passed in order to apply for a university or other institutions of higher learning.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.otouczelnie.pl/artykul/4578/Matura-2020-i-wszystko-co-trzeba-o-niej-wiedziec|title=MATURA 2020 &#124; wymagania na STUDIA &#124; jak wygląda &#124; terminy|website=otouczelnie.pl}}</ref>

The standards of [[Higher education|higher]] [[tertiary education]] are imposed by the [[Ministry of Science and Higher Education (Poland)|Ministry of Science and Higher Education]]. In Poland, there are over 500 university-level institutions,<ref>Central Statistical Office: [http://www.stat.gov.pl/cps/rde/xbcr/gus/PUBL_E_szkoly_wyzsze_2008.pdf Studenci szkół wyższych (łącznie z cudzoziemcami) na dzień 30 XI 2008.] Number of students at Poland's institutions of higher education, as of 30 November 2008. Retrieved 13 June 2012. Archived at [https://web.archive.org/web/20081028221046/http://www.stat.gov.pl/cps/rde/xbcr/gus/PUBL_maly_rocznik_statystyczny_2008.pdf Archive.org] on 28 October 2008. {{in lang|pl}}</ref> with technical, medical, economic, agricultural, pedagogical, theological, musical, maritime and military faculties.<ref name="studies.info">{{cite web|url=https://studies.info/en/country/poland|title=Study in Poland|website=studies.info|access-date=27 March 2019}}</ref> The [[University of Warsaw]] and [[Warsaw Polytechnic]], the [[University of Wrocław]], [[Adam Mickiewicz University in Poznań]] and the [[Gdańsk University of Technology|University of Technology in Gdańsk]] are among the most prominent.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://ranking.perspektywy.pl/2019/ranking-uczelni-akademickich|title=Ranking Uczelni Akademickich – Ranking Szkół Wyższych PERSPEKTYWY 2019|website=ranking.perspektywy.pl}}</ref> There are three conventional [[academic degree]]s in Poland – ''[[Licentiate (degree)|licencjat]]'' or ''[[Bachelor's degree|inżynier]]'' (first cycle qualification), ''[[magister (degree)|magister]]'' (second cycle qualification) and ''[[PhD|doktor]]'' (third cycle qualification).<ref name="The impact of the 1999 education reform in Poland" />

In 2018, the [[Programme for International Student Assessment]], coordinated by the [[Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development]], ranked Poland's educational system higher than the OECD average; the study showed that students in Poland perform better academically than in most OECD countries.<ref>https://www.oecd.org/pisa/publications/PISA2018_CN_POL.pdf</ref>

== Culture ==
{{Main|Culture of Poland}}
[[File:Sigismund's Chapel 01 AB.jpg|thumb|right|The [[Coat of arms of Poland|Polish White Eagle]] is Poland's enduring [[National symbols of Poland|national and cultural symbol]]]]
The culture of Poland is closely connected with its intricate 1,000-year [[History of Poland|history]] and forms an important constituent in [[western world|western civilization]].<ref name="amazon" /> The Poles take great [[Patriotism|pride]] in their national identity which is often associated with the colours white and red, and exuded by the expression ''biało-czerwoni'' ("whitereds").<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://sjp.pwn.pl/slowniki/Bia%C5%82o-Czerwoni.html|title=Biało-Czerwoni – definicja, synonimy, przykłady użycia|website=sjp.pwn.pl}}</ref> National symbols, chiefly the crowned [[white-tailed eagle]], are often visible on clothing, insignia and emblems. The appreciation of Poland's traditions and cultural heritage is commonly known as [[Polonophilia]].<ref>{{cite book| title= Rocznik Biblioteki Narodowej |date= 2004 |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/Rocznik_Biblioteki_Narodowej/-BVOAQAAMAAJ?hl=en&gbpv=0&bsq=polonofil%20definicja |location=Poland |language= pl |publisher=Biblioteka Narodowa |page=301 |isbn=978-83-7009-420-1}}</ref>

With origins in the customs of the tribal [[Lechites]], over time the culture of Poland has been influenced by its connection to [[Western culture]] and trends, as well as developing its own unique traditions such as [[Sarmatism]].<ref name="MFA" /> The people of Poland have traditionally been seen as hospitable to artists from abroad and eager to follow cultural and artistic trends popular in foreign countries, for instance, the 16th- and 17th-century tradition of [[coffin portraits]] (''portret trumienny'') was only observed in Poland and [[Roman Egypt]].<ref>{{Cite journal|title=The Coffin Portrait and Celebration of Death in Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth in the Modern Period|first=Bartłomiej|last=Łyczak|date=1 January 2011|journal=IKON|volume=4|pages=233–242|doi=10.1484/J.IKON.5.100699}}</ref> In the 19th and 20th centuries the Polish focus on cultural advancement often took precedence over political and economic activity. These factors have contributed to the versatile nature of Polish art.<ref name="MFA" />

The architectural monuments of great importance are protected by the [[National Heritage Board of Poland]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.nid.pl/pl/Dla_specjalistow/Badania_i_dokumentacja/zabytki-nieruchome/|title=Zabytki nieruchome|website=www.nid.pl}}</ref> Over 100 of the country's most significant tangible wonders were enlisted onto the [[List of Historic Monuments (Poland)|Historic Monuments Register]],<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.nid.pl/pl/Dla_wlascicieli_i_zarzadcow/Aktualnosci/news.php?ID=4114|title=Album "100 pomników historii"|website=www.nid.pl}}</ref> with further 17 being recognized by [[UNESCO]] as World Heritage Sites. Poland is renowned for its brick Gothic castles, [[granary|granaries]] and churches as well as diversely-styled [[tenements]], market squares and [[Ratusz|town halls]]. The majority of Polish cities founded on [[Magdeburg rights|Magdeburg Law]] in the [[Middle Ages]] evolved around central marketplaces, a distinguishable urban characteristic which can be observed to this day.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.szkolnictwo.pl/szukaj,Prawo_magdeburskie|title=prawo magdeburskie – Szkolnictwo.pl|website=www.szkolnictwo.pl}}</ref> Medieval and Renaissance [[cloth hall]]s were once an abundant feature of many towns.<ref>{{cite book |last = Szolginia|first = Witold|title = Architektura|publisher = Sigma NOT|location = Warsaw|date = 1992| page = 152| isbn = 978-83-85001-89-8}}</ref>

=== Holidays and traditions ===
{{see also|Christmas in Poland}}
[[File:Celebración de Todos los Santos, cementerio de la Santa Cruz, Gniezno, Polonia, 2017-11-01, DD 10-12 HDR.jpg|thumb|left|[[All Saints' Day]] on 1 November is one of the most important public holidays in Poland.]]
There are 13 government-approved annual public holidays – [[New Year]] on 1 January, [[Epiphany (holiday)|Three Kings' Day]] on 6 January, [[Easter Sunday]] and [[Easter Monday]], [[International Workers' Day|Labour Day]] on 1 May, [[3 May Constitution Day|Constitution Day]] on 3 May, [[Pentecost]], [[Feast of Corpus Christi|Corpus Christi]], [[Assumption of Mary|Feast of the Assumption]] on 15 August, [[All Saints' Day]] on 1 November, [[Independence Day (Poland)|Independence Day]] on 11 November and [[Christmas]]tide on 25 and 26 December.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://isap.sejm.gov.pl/isap.nsf/DocDetails.xsp?id=WDU20150000090|title=Obwieszczenie Marszałka Sejmu Rzeczypospolitej Polskiej z dnia 19 grudnia 2014 r. w sprawie ogłoszenia jednolitego tekstu ustawy o dniach wolnych od pracy|website=isap.sejm.gov.pl}}</ref>

Particular traditions and superstitious customs observed in Poland are not found elsewhere in Europe. Though [[Christmas Eve]] (''[[Wigilia]]'') is not a public holiday, it remains the most memorable day of the entire year. [[Christmas trees|Trees]] are decorated on 24 December, hay is placed under the tablecloth to resemble Jesus' [[manger]], [[Christmas wafer]]s (''opłatek'') are shared between gathered guests and a [[Twelve-dish Christmas Eve supper|twelve-dish meatless supper]] is served that same evening when the [[Star of Bethlehem|first star]] appears.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://wegorzewo.wm.pl/407437,Oplatek-i-pierwsza-gwiazdka-czyli-wigilijne-tradycje.html|title=Opłatek i pierwsza gwiazdka czyli wigilijne tradycje|website=wegorzewo.wm.pl}}</ref> An empty plate and seat are symbolically left at the table for an unexpected guest.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://culture.pl/en/article/why-do-poles-leave-one-chair-empty-on-christmas-eve|title=Why Do Poles Leave One Chair Empty on Christmas Eve?|website=Culture.pl}}</ref> On occasion, [[Christmas carols|carolers]] journey around smaller towns with a folk [[Turoń]] creature until the [[Lent]] period.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://dobryslownik.pl/slowo/turo%C5%84/57454/|title=turoń – słownik języka polskiego i poradnia językowa – Dobry słownik|website=DobrySłownik.pl}}</ref>

A widely-popular [[pączki|doughnut]] and sweet pastry feast occurs on [[Fat Thursday]], usually 52 days prior to [[Easter]].<ref name="auto">{{Cite book|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=eUrSDwAAQBAJ&q=t%C5%82usty+czwartek&pg=PA112|title=English Translations of Korczak's Children's Fiction: A Linguistic Perspective|first=Michał|last=Borodo|date=22 February 2020|publisher=Springer Nature|isbn=978-3-030-38117-2|via=Google Books}}</ref> [[Easter egg|Eggs]] for [[Easter Sunday|Holy Sunday]] are painted and placed in decorated [[święconka|baskets]] that are previously blessed by clergymen in churches on [[Easter Saturday]]. Easter Monday is celebrated with pagan ''[[śmigus-dyngus|dyngus]]'' festivities, where the youth is engaged in water fights.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://culture.pl/en/article/smigus-dyngus-polands-national-water-fight-day|title=Śmigus-Dyngus: Poland's National Water Fight Day|website=Culture.pl}}</ref><ref name="auto"/>

Cemeteries and graves of the deceased are annually visited by family members on All Saints' Day; tombstones are cleaned as a sign of respect and candles are lit to honour the dead on an unprecedented scale.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.xperiencepoland.com/all-saints-day-poland/|title=Summer in Warsaw &#124; Things You Can Do Only in Summer|date=21 October 2018}}</ref>

=== Music ===
{{Main|Music of Poland}}
{{multiple image
 | align = right
 | image1 = Frederic Chopin photo.jpeg
 | width1 = 150
 | alt1 = Fryderyk Chopin
 | caption1 = [[Frédéric Chopin|Fryderyk Chopin]] was a renowned classical composer and virtuoso pianist.
 | image2 = Optreden Arthur Rubinstein in Concertgebouw, Bestanddeelnr 913-5228.jpg
 | width2 = 142
 | alt2 = Artur Rubinstein 
 | caption2 = [[Arthur Rubinstein|Artur Rubinstein]] was one of the greatest concert pianists of the 20th century.
}}

Artists from Poland, including famous musicians such as [[Frédéric Chopin|Chopin]], [[Artur Rubinstein|Rubinstein]], [[Ignacy Jan Paderewski|Paderewski]], [[Krzysztof Penderecki|Penderecki]] and [[Henryk Wieniawski|Wieniawski]], and traditional, regionalized [[folk music|folk composers]] create a lively and diverse music scene, which even recognizes its own music genres, such as [[sung poetry]] and [[disco polo]].<ref>{{cite book |title=Individuals and Their Social Context |date=31 December 2018 |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/Individuals_and_Their_Social_Contexts/T2YLEAAAQBAJ?hl=en&gbpv=0 |location=Poland |publisher=Institute of Political Studies Polish Academy of Sciences |page=160 |isbn=978-83-65972-34-7}}</ref>

The origins of Polish music can be traced to the 13th century; manuscripts have been found in [[Stary Sącz]] containing [[polyphony|polyphonic]] compositions related to the Parisian [[Notre Dame School]]. Other early compositions, such as the melody of ''[[Bogurodzica]]'' and ''[[God Is Born]]'' (a coronation [[Polonaise (dance)|polonaise tune]] for Polish kings by an unknown composer), may also date back to this period, however, the first known notable composer, [[Mikołaj z Radomia|Nicholas of Radom]], lived in the 15th century. [[Diomedes Cato]], a native-born Italian who lived in Kraków, became a renowned lutenist at the court of Sigismund III; he not only imported some of the musical styles from southern Europe but blended them with native folk music.<ref name="The Music Courts of the Polish Vasas" />

{{Listen
| header      = '''[[Fryderyk Chopin]]'''
| filename    = Frederic Chopin - mazurka no. 4 in a minor, op. 17.ogg
| title       = Mazurka no. 4 in a minor, op. 17
| description = [[Mazurka]] ({{lang-pl|mazurek}}), stylized [[folk dance]] in [[triple meter]] (1832), commemorating the [[November Uprising]]
| help        = no
| pos         = left
}}

In the 17th and 18th centuries, Polish baroque composers wrote [[liturgical music]] and secular compositions such as [[concerto]]s and [[sonata]]s for voices or instruments. At the end of the 18th century, Polish classical music evolved into national forms like the [[polonaise (dance)|polonaise]]. [[Wojciech Bogusławski]] is accredited with composing the first Polish national [[opera]], titled ''[[:pl:Krakowiacy i Górale|Krakowiacy i Górale]]'', which premiered in 1794.<ref>{{cite book |last=Wolff |first=Larry |date=9 January 2012 |title=The Idea of Galicia; History and Fantasy in Habsburg Political Culture |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/The_Idea_of_Galicia/tgjQYHn7BTkC?hl=en&gbpv=0 |publisher=Stanford University Press |page=57 |isbn=978-0-8047-7429-1}}</ref>

Traditional Polish folk music has had a major effect on the works of many Polish composers, and no more so than on Fryderyk Chopin, a widely recognised national hero of the arts. All of Chopin's [[List of compositions by Frédéric Chopin|works]] involve the piano and are technically demanding, emphasising nuance and expressive depth. As a great composer, Chopin invented the [[musical form]] known as the [[ballade (classical music)#Instrumental ballades|instrumental ballade]] and made major innovations to the [[piano sonata]], [[mazurka]], [[waltz]], [[nocturne]], [[polonaise (dance)|polonaise]], [[étude]], [[impromptu]] and [[prelude (music)|prélude]], he was also the composer of a number of polonaises which borrowed heavily from traditional Polish folk music. It is largely thanks to him that such pieces gained great popularity throughout Europe during the 19th century. Several Polish composers such as [[Karol Szymanowski|Szymanowski]] drew inspiration from Chopin's folk-influenced style. Nowadays the most distinctive folk music can be heard in the towns and villages of the mountainous south, particularly in the region surrounding the winter resort town of [[Zakopane]].<ref>{{cite book |last=Downes |first=Stephen |date=9 March 2016 |title=The Szymanowski Companion |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/The_Szymanowski_Companion/AHu1CwAAQBAJ?hl=en&gbpv=0 |publisher=Taylor & Francis |page=89 |isbn=978-1-317-01444-7}}</ref>

{{Listen
| header      = '''[[Ballades (Chopin)|Ballade form]] invented by [[Frédéric Chopin|Chopin]]'''.<ref>{{cite web | url=http://www.chopinmusic.net/works/ballades/ | title=Ballades (Frédéric Chopin) | work=Chopin Music | date=2004–13 | access-date=7 January 2013 | author=Nico Paul | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130116214304/http://www.chopinmusic.net/works/ballades/ | archive-date=16 January 2013 | url-status=dead}}</ref>
| filename    = Frederic Chopin - ballade no. 3 in a flat major, op. 47.ogg
| title       = Ballade no. 3 in a-flat major, op. 47
| description = Inspired by poems of [[Adam Mickiewicz]]
| help        = no
| pos         = right
}}

Poland today has an active music scene, with the jazz and metal genres being particularly popular among the contemporary populace. Polish jazz musicians such as [[Krzysztof Komeda]] created a unique style, which was most famous in the 1960s and 1970s and continues to be popular to this day. Poland has also become a major venue for large-scale music festivals, chief among which are the [[Open'er Festival]], [[Opole Festival]] and [[Sopot Festival]].<ref>{{cite book |last=Guillain |first=Charlotte |date=2012 |title=Poland |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/Poland/PlF8Xr90I1cC?hl=en&gbpv=0 |publisher=Raintree |page=29 |isbn=978-1-4062-2826-7}}</ref>

=== Art ===
{{Main|Art in Poland|Young Poland|List of Polish artists}}
[[File:Lady with an Ermine - Leonardo da Vinci - Google Art Project.jpg|thumb|left|upright=0.8|''[[Lady with an Ermine]]'' (1490) by [[Leonardo da Vinci]]. Though not Polish in its origin, the painting symbolizes Poland's cultural heritage and is among the country's most precious treasures.]]

Art in Poland has always reflected European trends while maintaining its unique character. The [[Kraków Academy of Fine Arts]], later developed by [[Jan Matejko]], produced monumental portrayals of customs and significant events in Polish history.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://culture.pl/en/place/jan-matejko-academy-of-fine-arts|title=Jan Matejko Academy of Fine Arts – Place |publisher=Culture.pl|access-date=31 August 2017}}</ref> Other institutions such as the [[Academy of Fine Arts in Warsaw]] were more innovative and focused on both historical and contemporary styles.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://asp.waw.pl/eng/history/|title=History|access-date=31 August 2017}}</ref> Notable art academies include the [[Cracow School of Art and Fashion Design|Kraków School of Art and Fashion Design]], [[Art Academy of Szczecin]], [[University of Fine Arts in Poznań]] and the [[Eugeniusz Geppert Academy of Fine Arts|Geppert Academy of Fine Arts in Wrocław]].

Perhaps the most prominent and internationally admired Polish artist was [[Tamara de Lempicka]], who specialized in the style of [[Art Deco]].<ref>{{cite book|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=QYHwLta1SooC&pg=PA47|title=Madonna: A Biography|first=Mary|last=Cross|date=31 August 2017|publisher=Greenwood Publishing Group|page=47|access-date=31 August 2017 |via=Google Books|isbn=978-0-313-33811-3}}</ref> Lempicka was described as "the first woman artist to become a glamour star."<ref>{{cite web |url=https://news.artnet.com/art-world/madonnas-art-collection-277970 |title=Take a Look Inside Madonna's $100 Million Blue-Chip Art Collection |work=artnet News |date=17 March 2015 |access-date=31 August 2017}}</ref> Another notable was [[Caziel]], born Zielenkiewicz, who represented [[Cubism]] and [[Abstraction]] in France and England.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.whitfordfineart.com/artists/52-caziel/biography/ |title=Caziel biography |website=Whitford Fine Art |access-date=31 August 2017}}</ref>

Prior to the 19th century only [[Daniel Schultz]] and Italian-born [[Marcello Bacciarelli]] had the privilege of being recognized abroad. The [[Young Poland]] movement witnessed the birth of modern Polish art, and engaged in a great deal of formal experimentation led by [[Jacek Malczewski]], [[Stanisław Wyspiański]], [[Józef Mehoffer]], and a group of Polish [[Impressionists]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://culture.pl/pl/tworca/jacek-malczewski|author=Jacek Malczewski| title= Twórca|publisher=Culture.pl|access-date=31 August 2017}}</ref> [[Stanisław Witkiewicz]] was an ardent supporter of [[Realism (arts)|Realism]], its main representative being [[Józef Marian Chełmoński|Józef Chełmoński]], while [[Artur Grottger]] specialized in [[Romanticism in Poland|Romanticism]]. Within historically-orientated circles, [[Henryk Siemiradzki]] dominated with his monumental [[Academic Art]] and [[Roman Empire|ancient Roman]] theme.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://culture.pl/en/artist/henryk-siemiradzki|author=Henryk Siemiradzki |title= Artist|publisher=Culture.pl|access-date=31 August 2017}}</ref>

[[File:3908viki Muzeum Narodowe. Fragment ekspozycji. Foto Barbara Maliszewska.jpg|thumb|Interior of the [[National Museum in Wrocław|National Museum]] in [[Wrocław]], which holds one of the largest collections of contemporary art in the country]]

Since the inter-war years, Polish art and documentary photography has enjoyed worldwide fame and in the 1960s the [[Polish School of Posters]] was formed.<ref name="MFA" /> Throughout the entire country, many national museum and art institutions hold valuable works by famous masters. Major museums in Poland include the [[National Museum, Warsaw|National Museum in Warsaw]], [[National Museum, Poznań|Poznań]], [[National Museum, Wrocław|Wrocław]], [[National Museum, Kraków|Kraków]], and [[National Museum, Gdańsk|Gdańsk]], as well as the [[Museum of John Paul II Collection]], and the [[Museum of King John III's Palace at Wilanów|Wilanów Museum]]. Important collections are also held at the [[Royal Castle, Warsaw|Royal Castle in Warsaw]], [[Wawel Castle]] and in the [[Palace on the Isle]]. Contemporary art galleries include [[Zachęta]], [[Ujazdów Castle|Ujazdów]], and [[MOCAK, Museum of Contemporary Art in Kraków|MOCAK]].<ref>{{cite web|last=Sarzyński|first=Piotr|date=2013-02-12|title=Ranking polskich galerii ze współczesną sztuką|url=https://www.polityka.pl/tygodnikpolityka/kultura/1535435,1,ranking-polskich-galerii-ze-wspolczesna-sztuka.read|access-date=2021-05-04|website=www.polityka.pl|language=pl}}</ref> The most distinguished painting of Poland is ''[[Lady with an Ermine]]'' by Leonardo da Vinci, held at the [[Czartoryski Museum]] in [[Kraków]]. Although not Polish, the work had a strong influence on Polish culture and has been often associated with Polish identity.<ref>{{cite web |title=Lady with an Ermine – by Leonardo Da Vinci |url=https://www.leonardodavinci.net/lady-with-an-ermine.jsp |website=LeonardoDaVinci.net}}</ref>

=== Architecture ===
<!-- This section is linked from redirect "Architecture of Poland" -->
{{main|Architecture of Poland}}

Polish cities and towns reflect a whole spectrum of European architectural styles. [[Romanesque architecture]] is represented by [[St. Andrew's Church, Kraków]], and [[St. Mary's Church, Gdańsk]], is characteristic for the [[Brick Gothic]] style found in Poland. Richly decorated [[attic style|attics]] and [[arcade (architecture)|arcade]] [[loggia]]s are the common elements of the Polish Renaissance architecture,<ref name="szydlowiec" /><ref name="RENAISSANCE CULTURAL BACKGROUND" /> as evident in the [[Poznań City Hall|City Hall]] in Poznań. For some time the late renaissance style known as [[mannerism]], most notably in the [[Cracow Bishops' Palace in Kielce|Bishop's Palace]] in [[Kielce]], coexisted with the early baroque style, typified in the [[Saints Peter and Paul Church, Kraków|Church of Saints Peter and Paul in Kraków]].<ref>{{cite book |last=Miłobędzki |first=Adam |date=1994 |title=The architecture of Poland : a chapter of the European heritage |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/Architektura_Ziem_Polski/QAMtAQAAIAAJ?hl=en&gbpv=0&bsq=pa%C5%82ac%20biskup%C3%B3w%20kielce%20manieryzm |location=Poland |language=pl |publisher=International Cultural Centre-Międzynarodowe Centrum Kultury w Krakowie |pages=52–56 |isbn=978-83-85739-14-2}}</ref>

{{multiple image
 | align = left
 | image1 = St Mary's Krakow.jpg
 | width1 = 161
 | alt1 = Saint Mary's Church in Kraków
 | caption1 = [[St. Mary's Basilica, Kraków|St. Mary's Basilica]] on the [[Main Market Square, Kraków|Main Market Square]] in [[Kraków]] is an example of [[Brick Gothic]] architecture
 | image2 = Ayuntamiento, Poznan, Polonia, 2014-09-18, DD 67-72 HDR.jpg 
 | width2 = 140
 | alt2 = Poznań City Hall
 | caption2 = [[Ratusz]], the 16th-century [[Renaissance in Poland|Renaissance]] City Hall in [[Poznań]] designed by Italian architects
}}

History has not been kind to Poland's architectural monuments. Nonetheless, a number of ancient structures have survived: castles, churches, and stately homes, often unique in the regional or European context. Some of them have been painstakingly restored, like [[Wawel Castle]], or completely reconstructed, including the [[Warsaw Old Town|Old Town]] and [[Royal Castle in Warsaw|Royal Castle]] of Warsaw and the Old Town of [[Gdańsk]].<ref>{{cite book |last=Centroni |first=Alessandra |date=3 January 2016 |title=Restauro e ricostruzione |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/Restauro_e_ricostruzione/vXJTCwAAQBAJ?hl=en&gbpv=0 |location=Italy |publisher=Gangemi Editore |page=51 |isbn=978-88-492-9191-9}}</ref>

The architecture of Gdańsk is mostly of the [[Hanseatic League|Hanseatic]] variety, a Gothic style common among the former trading cities along the [[Baltic Sea]] and in the northern part of Central Europe. The architectural style of [[Wrocław]] is mainly representative of German architecture since it was for centuries located within the Holy Roman Empire. The centres of [[Kazimierz Dolny]] and [[Sandomierz]] on the [[Vistula]] are good examples of well-preserved medieval towns. Poland's ancient capital, [[Kraków]], ranks among the best-preserved [[Gothic architecture|Gothic]] and Renaissance urban complexes in Europe.<ref>{{cite book |last=Spirou |first=Costas |date=13 January 2011 |title=Urban Tourism and Urban Change |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/Urban_Tourism_and_Urban_Change/1dOsAgAAQBAJ?hl=en&gbpv=0 |publisher=Taylor & Francis |page=64 |isbn=978-1-136-85903-8}}</ref>

The second half of the 17th century is marked by [[baroque]] architecture. Side towers, such as those of [[Branicki Palace, Białystok|Branicki Palace]] in Białystok, are typical for the Polish baroque. The classical [[Silesian architecture|Silesian baroque]] is represented by the [[University of Wrocław|University in Wrocław]]. The profuse decorations of the [[Branicki Palace, Warsaw|Branicki Palace]] in Warsaw are characteristic of the [[rococo]] style. The centre of Polish classicism was Warsaw under the rule of the last Polish king [[Stanisław II Augustus]].<ref>{{cite journal|last=Stanley|first=John|year=2004|title=Reviewed Work: Literary Activities and Attitudes in the Stanislavian Age in Poland (1764–1795): A Social System? by Jan I.J. van der Meer|journal=Canadian Slavonic Papers|volume=46|issue=1/2|pages=226–229|jstor=40870954}}</ref>
The [[Palace on the Isle]] is a chief example of Polish [[neoclassical architecture]]. [[Lublin Castle]] represents the [[Gothic Revival architecture|Gothic Revival]] style in architecture,<ref>{{cite book |last=Żywicki |first=Jerzy |date=1998 |title=Architektura neogotycka na Lubelszczyźnie |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/Architektura_neogotycka_na_Lubelszczy%C5%BAn/__gsAQAAIAAJ?hl=en&gbpv=0&bsq=zamek%20lublin%20neogotyk |location=Poland |language=pl |publisher=Regionalny Ośrodek Studiów i Ochrony Środowiska Kulturowego w Lublinie |isbn=978-83-908495-0-8}}</ref> while the [[Izrael Poznański Palace]] in [[Łódź]] is an example of [[eclecticism]].<ref>{{cite book |last=Marcinek |first=Roman |date=2002 |title=Polska. Dwory, zamki, pałace. |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/Polska/3bIVAQAAIAAJ?hl=en&gbpv=0&bsq=pa%C5%82ac%20pozna%C5%84skiego%20eklektyzm |location=Poland |language=pl |publisher=Kluszczyński |isbn=978-83-88080-71-5}}</ref>

[[File:Kazimierz Dolny Market Square.jpg|thumb|right|[[Kazimierz Dolny]], the town exemplifies traditional provincial Polish folk architecture.]]
