Traditional folk architecture in the villages and small towns scattered across the vast Polish countryside was characterized by its extensive use of wood and [[brick|red brick]] as primary building materials, common for Central Europe.<ref>{{cite book |last=Rączka |first=Jan Władysław |date=2001 |title=Walka o polski styl narodowy w architekturze |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/Walka_o_polski_styl_narodowy_w_architekt/zb8VAQAAIAAJ?hl=en&gbpv=0&bsq=architektura%20polski%20drewno%20ceg%C5%82a |location=Poland |language=pl |publisher=Politechnika Krakowska |isbn=978-83-7242-153-1}}</ref> Some of the best preserved and oldest structures include ancient stone temples in [[Silesia]] and fortified wooden [[Wooden churches of Southern Lesser Poland|churches]] across southeastern Poland in the [[Beskids]] and [[Bieszczady Mountains|Bieszczady]] regions of the Carpathian mountains.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://whc.unesco.org/en/list/1053|title=Wooden Churches of Southern Małopolska|first=UNESCO World Heritage|last=Centre|website=whc.unesco.org}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://whc.unesco.org/en/list/1424|title=Wooden Tserkvas of the Carpathian Region in Poland and Ukraine|first=UNESCO World Heritage|last=Centre|website=whc.unesco.org}}</ref> Numerous examples of secular structures such as [[Dwór (manor house)|Polish manor houses]] (''dworek''), [[farmhouses]] ([[:pl:chata|''chata'']]), [[Granary|granaries]], [[Gristmill|mills]], [[barn]]s and country inns ([[:pl:karczma|''karczma'']]) can still be found in some Polish regions. However, traditional construction methods faded in the early-mid 20th century, when Poland's population experienced a [[Urbanisation|demographic shift to urban dwelling]] away from the countryside.<ref>{{cite book |last=Centroni |first=Alessandra |date=3 January 2016 |title=Restauro e ricostruzione |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/Restauro_e_ricostruzione/vXJTCwAAQBAJ?hl=en&gbpv=0 |location=Italy |publisher=Gangemi Editore |page=121 |isbn=978-88-492-9191-9}}</ref>

=== Literature ===
{{Main|Polish literature|History of philosophy in Poland}}

The earliest examples of [[Polish literature]] date to the 12th century,<ref name="LIT01" /> when Poland's official language was [[Latin]], and early published works were predominantly written by foreigners. [[Gallus Anonymus]], a [[monk]] of disputed origin, was the first chronicler who meticulously described Poland's culture, language and territories in ''[[Gesta principum Polonorum]]'' (c. 1112–1118).<ref>{{cite web|url=http://pamiecpolski.archiwa.gov.pl/objects/the-zamojski-codex|title=The Chronicle of Gallus Anonymus. The Zamojski Codex|first=Katarzyna|last=Szewczyk|website=pamiecpolski.archiwa.gov.pl|access-date=24 May 2017}}</ref> Latin remained the principal tool of literary expression in Poland until the 18th century, when it was replaced in favour of Polish and [[French language|French]]. Historically, Polish literature concentrated extensively around the themes of true [[drama]] and [[Poem|poetic]]-expressive romanticism than on [[Literary fiction|fiction]]. [[Patriotism]], [[spirituality]] and [[aphorism]]s were paramount and political or social [[allegory|allegories]] were common [[moral]] narratives.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.britannica.com/art/Polish-literature|title=Polish literature – Romanticism|website=Encyclopedia Britannica}}</ref><ref>{{Cite book|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=aCRm0K8Y-2sC&q=polish+literature+patriotic+morals&pg=PA184|title=Values in the Polish Cultural Tradition|first=Leon|last=Dyczewski|date=29 July 2002|publisher=CRVP|isbn=978-1-56518-142-7|via=Google Books}}</ref>

{{multiple image
 | align = left
 | image1 = Adam Mickiewicz.PNG
 | width1 = 158
 | alt1 = Adam Mickiewicz
 | caption1 = [[Adam Mickiewicz]] was an untiring promoter of Poland's culture and heritage. His [[Epic poetry|national epic poem]] ''[[Pan Tadeusz]]'' is considered a masterpiece of [[Polish literature]].
 | image2 = Joseph Conrad.PNG
 | width2 = 132
 | alt2 = Joseph Conrad-Korzeniowski
 | caption2 = [[Joseph Conrad]], one of the greatest novelists of all time. He was the author of popular books such as ''[[Nostromo]]'' and ''[[Heart of Darkness]]''.
}}

The first documented phrase in the [[Polish language]] reads "''Day ut ia pobrusa, a ti poziwai''" ("Let me grind, and you take a rest"), reflecting the use of [[quern-stone]] in early Poland.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://scienceinpoland.pap.pl/en/news/news,370714,the-manuscript-with-the-first-ever-sentence-in-polish-has-be-digitalized.html|title=The manuscript with the first ever sentence in Polish has {{sic|be|nolink=y}} digitalized – News – Science & Scholarship in Poland|first=Ideo Sp. z o.o. -|last=www.ideo.pl|website=scienceinpoland.pap.pl|access-date=24 May 2017|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170821212328/http://scienceinpoland.pap.pl/en/news/news,370714,the-manuscript-with-the-first-ever-sentence-in-polish-has-be-digitalized.html|archive-date=21 August 2017}}</ref> The phrase was recorded by an abbot in the Latin-based ''[[Liber fundationis]]'' from 1269 to 1273, which outlined the history of a [[Cistercian]] monastery in the [[Silesia]]n village of [[Henryków, Lower Silesian Voivodeship|Henryków]]. The sentence has been included in the [[Memory of the World Programme|UNESCO Memory of World Register]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://poland.pl/tourism/unesco-sites/first-sentence-polish-unesco-register/|title=The first sentence in Polish in the UNESCO register|website=#Poland|access-date=24 May 2017}}</ref> The oldest extant manuscript of fine [[prose]] in [[Old Polish language|Old Polish]] is the ''[[Holy Cross Sermons]]'', and the earliest religious text is the [[Bible of Queen Sophia]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://polishlibraries.pl/article.php?a=14|title=Polish Libraries – Wiesław Wydra: The Oldest Extant Prose Text in the Polish language. The Phenomenon of the Holy Cross Sermons.|website=polishlibraries.pl|access-date=24 May 2017}}</ref> One of the first printing houses was established by [[Kasper Straube]] in the 1470s, while [[Jan Haller]] was considered the pioneer of commercial print in Poland. Haller's [[Almanach cracoviense ad annum 1474|Calendarium cracoviense]], an astronomical wall calendar from 1474, is Poland's oldest surviving print.<ref>{{cite book|last1=Carter|first1=F.W.|title=Trade and Urban Development in Poland: An Economic Geography of Cracow, from Its Origins to 1795|date=2006|publisher=Cambridge University Press|isbn=978-0-521-02438-9|page=364}}</ref>

The tradition of extending Polish historiography in Latin was subsequently inherited by [[Vincent Kadłubek]], Bishop of [[Kraków]] in the 13th century, and [[Jan Długosz]] in the 15th century.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.polskieradio.pl/39/156/Artykul/1392738,Wincenty-Kadlubek-pierwszy-rodzimy-kronikarz|title=Wincenty Kadłubek – pierwszy rodzimy kronikarz|access-date=24 May 2017}}</ref> This practice, however, was abandoned by [[Jan Kochanowski]], who became one of the first [[Renaissance in Poland|Polish Renaissance]] authors to write most of his works in Polish, along with [[Nicholas Rey]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://fp.amu.edu.pl/dwujezycznosc-w-tworczosci-jana-kochanowskiego/|title=Dwujęzyczność w twórczości Jana Kochanowskiego|website=fp.amu.edu.pl}}</ref> Other writers of the Polish Renaissance include [[Johannes Dantiscus]], [[Andreus Fricius Modrevius]], [[Matthias Sarbievius]], [[Piotr Skarga]] and [[Klemens Janicki|Klemens "Ianicius" Janicki]], who was laureled by the [[Pope]]. The leading figure of the Polish Reformation was theologian and writer [[John Laski]], who, with the permission of King [[Edward VI of England]], created the European Protestant Congregation of London in 1550.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://reformowani.org.pl/teologia/818-jan-laski|title=Jan Łaski – Parafia Ewangelicko-Reformowana w Warszawie|website=Parafia Ewangelicko-Reformowana w Warszawie|access-date=24 May 2017}}</ref>

[[File:Banquet in Nero's palace - Ulpiano Checa y Sanz.jpg|thumb|right|upright=1|''Banquet in Nero's Palace'', an illustration from a 1910 print of ''[[Quo Vadis (novel)|Quo Vadis]]'', a historical novel written by [[Nobel Prize in Literature|Nobel Prize laureate]] [[Henryk Sienkiewicz]]]]

During the [[Polish Baroque|Baroque]] era, the [[Jesuits]] greatly influenced Polish literature and literary techniques, often relying on God and religious matters.<ref>{{cite book |url=http://www.ucpress.edu/book.php?isbn=9780520233577 |title=Propaganda and the Jesuit Baroque |author=Evonne Levy |date=April 2004 |publisher=University of California Press |isbn=978-0-520-23357-7 |access-date=24 May 2017}}</ref> The leading baroque poet was [[Jan Andrzej Morsztyn]], who incorporated [[Marinism]] into his publications. [[Jan Chryzostom Pasek]], also a respected baroque writer, is mostly remembered for his tales and memoirs reflecting [[Sarmatism|sarmatian]] culture in the [[Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth]].<ref>{{cite encyclopedia |url=https://www.britannica.com/biography/Jan-Chryzostom-Pasek|title=Jan Chryzostom Pasek |encyclopedia=Encyclopædia Britannica|access-date=24 May 2017}}</ref> Subsequently, the [[Polish Enlightenment]] was headed by [[Samuel Linde]], [[Hugo Kołłątaj]], [[Izabela Czartoryska]] and [[Julian Ursyn Niemcewicz]]. In 1776, [[Ignacy Krasicki]] composed the first milestone novel entitled ''[[The Adventures of Mr. Nicholas Wisdom]]''.<ref>{{cite book|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=Ue3cAgAAQBAJ&pg=PA166 |title=The Encyclopedia of the Novel |editor=Peter Melville Logan |others=Associate editors:Olakunle George, Susan Hegeman, EfraÃn Kristal |year=2014|publisher=John Wiley & Sons|access-date=24 May 2017|via=Google Books|isbn=978-1-118-77907-1}}</ref>

Among the best known [[Romanticism in Poland|Polish Romantics]] are the "[[Three Bards]]" – the three [[national poets]] active in the [[Partitions of Poland|age of foreign partitions]] – [[Adam Mickiewicz]], [[Juliusz Słowacki]] and [[Zygmunt Krasiński]].<ref>{{cite book|author=Eunice L. Blavascunas|title=The Peasant and Communist Past in the Making of an Ecological Region: Podlasie, Poland|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=ZsEzM8Gbl68C&pg=PA98|year=2008|isbn=978-0-549-65633-3|page=98}}</ref> The narrative poem ''[[Pan Tadeusz]]'' by Mickiewicz is Poland's [[national epic]] and a compulsory reading (''lektura'') in the country's schools.<ref>{{cite book |last=Nyczek |first=Tadeusz |date=2005 |title=Lektury obowiązkowe |location=Poland |publisher=Społeczny Instytut Wydawniczy "Znak" |isbn=978-83-240-0549-9}}</ref> [[Joseph Conrad]], the son of dramatist [[Apollo Korzeniowski]], came to fame with his English-language novels and stories that are informed with elements of the [[History of Poland|Polish national experience]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.josephconradsociety.org/|title=The Joseph Conrad Society (UK) Official Website|work=josephconradsociety.org|access-date=10 February 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://josephconrad.org/|title=The Joseph Conrad Society of America|work=josephconrad.org|access-date=10 February 2016}}</ref> Conrad's ''[[Heart of Darkness]]'', ''[[Nostromo]]'' and ''[[Lord Jim]]'' are believed to be one of the finest works ever written, placing him among the greatest novelists of all time.<ref>{{cite encyclopedia|url=https://www.britannica.com/biography/Joseph-Conrad|title=Joseph Conrad |encyclopedia=Encyclopædia Britannica|access-date=24 May 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://rawlangs.com/2012/12/27/multilingualism-and-literature-10-authors-who-write-in-other-languages/|title=Multilingualism and literature: 10 authors who write in other languages|date=27 December 2012|access-date=24 May 2017|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170404060256/http://rawlangs.com/2012/12/27/multilingualism-and-literature-10-authors-who-write-in-other-languages/|archive-date=4 April 2017}}</ref> Modern Polish literature is versatile, with its [[Fantasy literature|fantasy]] genre having been particularly praised.<ref>{{cite book |last=Booker |first=M. Keith |date=2020 |title=Historical Dictionary of Science Fiction Cinema |publisher=Rowman & Littlefield Publishers |page=261 |isbn=978-1-5381-3010-0}}</ref> The philosophical [[science-fiction|sci-fi]] novel ''[[Solaris (novel)|Solaris]]'' is an acclaimed example of [[Stanisław Lem|Stanisław Lem's]] literary legacy, whereas ''[[The Witcher]]'', a [[fantasy]] series by [[Andrzej Sapkowski]], is a much-celebrated work of contemporary Polish fiction.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://rynek-ksiazki.pl/aktualnosci/o-wiedzminie-i-wiedzmince/|title=O Wiedźminie i Wiedźmince|website=Rynek książki}}</ref>

In the 20th century, five Polish authors were awarded the [[Nobel Prize in Literature]] – [[Henryk Sienkiewicz]] for ''[[Quo Vadis (novel)|Quo Vadis]]'', [[Władysław Reymont]] for ''[[The Peasants]]'', [[Isaac Bashevis Singer]], [[Czesław Miłosz]] and [[Wisława Szymborska]].<ref name="Facts on the Nobel Prize in Literature" /><ref name="Szymborska's 'View': Small Truths Sharply Etched" /> In 2019, Polish author [[Olga Tokarczuk]] was awarded the Nobel Prize in Literature for the year 2018.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/entertainment-arts-49976107|title=Tokarczuk and Handke win Nobel Literature Prizes|work=BBC News|date=10 October 2019}}</ref>

=== Cuisine ===
{{Main|Polish cuisine}}
[[File:07425 Jahrmarkt in Sanok am 17 Juli 2011.jpg|thumb|left|Selection of hearty traditional comfort food from Poland including [[bigos]], [[cabbage roll]]s, [[żurek]], [[pierogi]], [[oscypek]] and specialty breads]]

Polish cuisine has evolved over the centuries to become highly eclectic due to Poland's history. Polish cuisine shares many similarities with other [[Central Europe]]an cuisines, especially [[German cuisine|German]] and [[Austrian cuisine|Austrian]]<ref name="Zibart" /> as well as [[Jewish cuisine|Jewish]],<ref name="ashkenazic" /> [[French cuisine|French]], [[Italian cuisine|Italian]] and [[Turkish cuisine|Turkish]] culinary traditions.<ref name="Jerzy_Pasikowski" /> Polish-styled cooking in other cultures is often referred to as ''cuisine à la polonaise''.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://journeyfromapolishkitchen.com/2015/11/10/a-la-polonaise/|title=à la Polonaise|first=Author|last=jadwiga49hjk|date=10 November 2015}}</ref>

Polish dishes are usually rich in meat, especially pork, chicken and beef (depending on the region), winter vegetables (sauerkraut cabbage in ''[[bigos]]''), and spices.<ref name="polishmeals" /> It is also characteristic in its use of various kinds of [[noodle]]s, the most notable of which are [[kluski]], as well as [[cereal]]s such as ''[[kasha]]'' (from the Polish word [[kasza]])<ref name="websters" /> and a variety of breads like the world-renowned [[bagel]]. Polish cuisine is hearty and uses a lot of cream and eggs. Festive meals such as the meatless Christmas Eve dinner (''[[Wigilia]]'') or [[Easter]] breakfast could take days to prepare in their entirety.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.polishcenter.org/Christmas/CHRISTMAS-ENG.htm |title=Traditional celebrations: Wigilia article from Pope John Paul II |website=Polish Center |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141130002746/http://www.polishcenter.org/Christmas/CHRISTMAS-ENG.htm |archive-date=30 November 2014 |publisher=Centrum Polonijne w Jorba Linda, California}}</ref>

[[File:Bagel Bialy.JPG|thumb|right|[[Bagel]]s, made from [[yeast]]ed [[wheat]] dough, originated in Poland.]]

The main course usually includes a serving of meat, such as roast, chicken, or ''[[kotlet schabowy]]'' (breaded pork cutlet), vegetables, side dishes and salads, including ''surówka'' {{IPA-pl|suˈrufka|}} – shredded root vegetables with lemon and sugar (carrot, celeriac, [[Searing|seared]] beetroot) or sauerkraut ({{lang-pl|kapusta kiszona}}, {{IPA-pl|kaˈpusta kʲiˈʂɔna|pron}}). The side dishes are usually potatoes, rice or cereal. Meals conclude with a dessert such as ''[[Cheesecake|sernik]]'' (cheesecake), ''[[makowiec (pastry)|makowiec]]'' ([[poppy seed]] pastry), or ''[[napoleonka]]'' ([[cream pie]]).<ref>{{cite book |last1=Steves |first1=Rick |last2=Hewitt |first2=Cameron |date=15 August 2017 |title=Rick Steves Snapshot Kraków, Warsaw & Gdańsk |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/Rick_Steves_Snapshot_Krak%C3%B3w_Warsaw_Gdan/T09IDgAAQBAJ?hl=en&gbpv=0 |publisher=Avalon Publishing |isbn=978-1-63121-624-4}}</ref>

The Polish national dishes are ''[[bigos]]'' {{IPA-pl|ˈbiɡɔs|}}; ''[[pierogi]]'' {{IPA-pl|pʲɛˈrɔɡʲi|}}; ''[[kielbasa]]''; ''[[kotlet schabowy]]'' {{IPA-pl|ˈkɔtlɛt sxaˈbɔvɨ|}} [[breaded cutlet]]; ''[[gołąbki]]'' {{IPA-pl|ɡɔˈwɔ̃pkʲi|}} [[cabbage roll]]s; ''[[zrazy]]'' {{IPA-pl|ˈzrazɨ|}} [[roulade]]; ''[[roast|pieczeń]]'' roast {{IPA-pl|ˈpʲɛt͡ʂɛɲ|}}; sour [[cucumber soup]] (''zupa ogórkowa'', {{IPA-pl|ˈzupa ɔɡurˈkɔva|pron}}); mushroom soup, (''zupa grzybowa'', {{IPA-pl|ˈzupa ɡʐɨˈbɔva|}} quite different from the North American [[cream of mushroom soup|cream of mushroom]]); ''zupa pomidorowa'' [[tomato soup]] {{IPA-pl|ˈzupa pɔmidɔˈrɔva|pron}};<ref name="Marc_Heine" /> ''[[rosół]]'' {{IPA-pl|ˈrɔɕuw|}} variety of meat broth; ''[[żurek]]'' {{IPA-pl|ˈʐurɛk|}} sour rye soup; ''[[flaki]]'' {{IPA-pl|ˈflakʲi|}} [[tripe soup]]; ''[[barszcz]]'' {{IPA-pl|barʂt͡ʂ|}} and ''[[chłodnik]]'' {{IPA-pl|ˈxwɔdɲik|}} among others.<ref name="Robert_Strybel" />

Traditional alcoholic beverages include honey [[Mead in Poland|mead]], widespread since the 13th century, [[Beer in Poland|beer]], wine and [[vodka]] (old Polish names include ''okowita'' and ''gorzała'').<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://sjp.pwn.pl/sjp/gorzala;2462442.html|title=gorzała – Słownik języka polskiego PWN|website=sjp.pwn.pl}}</ref> The world's first written mention of vodka originates from Poland.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://krps.pl/index.php?option=com_content&task=view&id=17&Itemid=27 |title=History of vodka production, at the official page of Polish Spirit Industry Association (KRPS), 2007 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070930131416/http://krps.pl/index.php?option=com_content&task=view&id=17&Itemid=27 |archive-date=30 September 2007}}</ref> The most popular alcoholic drinks at present are beer and wine which took over from vodka more popular in the years 1980–1998.<ref name="beverages" /> Tea remains common in Polish society since the 19th century, whilst coffee is drunk widely since the 18th century.<ref>{{cite book|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=UtA6-pyGJmMC&q=tea+19th+century+most+popular+in+poland&pg=PA692|title=Polish Heritage Cookery|first1=Robert|last1=Strybel|first2=Maria|last2=Strybel|date=31 March 2019|publisher=Hippocrene Books|access-date=31 March 2019|via=Google Books|isbn=978-0-7818-1124-8}}</ref> Other frequently consumed beverages include various mineral waters and juices, soft drinks popularized by the fast-food chains since the late 20th century, as well as [[buttermilk]], [[soured milk]] and [[kefir]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://culture.pl/en/article/a-mini-guide-to-polish-dairy|title=A Mini-Guide to Polish Dairy|website=Culture.pl|access-date=31 March 2019}}</ref>

=== Fashion and design ===
{{Further|Category:Polish fashion}}
[[File:Robe à la Polonaise MET DT11155.jpg|thumb|right|upright=.75|Traditional Polish ''[[Polonaise (clothing)|polonaise]]'' dresses, 1780–85]]

The particular clothing styles in Poland evolved with each century. In the 1600s high-class [[Szlachta|noblemen]] and [[magnate]]s developed a strong 
sympathy for [[Orientalism]], which was also common in other parts of Europe and became known as [[Sarmatism]].<ref name="visegradinsight.eu" /> The attire mediated between [[Western world|Western]] and [[Ottoman Empire|Ottoman]] styles<ref name="visegradinsight.eu">{{cite web |author=Miltiades Varvounis |date=26 February 2015 |url=http://visegradinsight.eu/sarmatism-and-polands-national-consciousness26022015/ |title="Sarmatism" and Poland's national consciousness |website=Visegrad Insight |access-date=24 May 2017}}</ref> and outfits included a [[żupan]], [[delia]], [[kontusz]], [[Pas kontuszowy|pas]], decorative [[karabela]] swords and less often [[turbans]] brought by foreign merchants. The period of Polish Sarmatism eventually faded in the wake of the 18th century.

The Polish national dress as well as the fashion and etiquette of Poland also reached the royal court at [[Versailles]] in the 1700s. French dresses inspired by Polish attire were called ''à la polonaise'', meaning "Polish-styled". The most famous example is the ''[[Polonaise (clothing)|robe à la polonaise]]'', a woman's garment with draped and swagged [[overskirt]], worn over an underskirt or [[petticoat]].<ref>{{cite encyclopedia |url=https://www.britannica.com/topic/polonaise-dress |title=Polonaise |encyclopedia=Encyclopædia Britannica |access-date=24 May 2017}}</ref> Another notable example is the [[Witzchoura]], a long mantle with collar and hood, which was possibly introduced by [[Napoleon]]'s Polish mistress [[Maria Walewska]]. The scope of influence also entailed furniture; rococo [[Polish bed]]s with [[Canopy bed|canopies]] became commonplace in French palaces during the 18th century.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=twGT8P_68lEC&q=lit+a+polonaise+marie+leszczynska&pg=PA586|title=The Wrightsman Collection. Vols. 1 and 2, Furniture, Gilt Bronze and Mounted Porcelain, Carpets|publisher=Metropolitan Museum of Art|via=Google Books}}</ref>

[[File:Reserved new concept.jpg|thumb|left|[[Reserved]] is Poland's most successful clothing store chain, operating in over 20 countries]]

Several Polish designers and stylists left a lifelong legacy of beauty inventions and [[cosmetics]], most notable being [[Maksymilian Faktorowicz]] and [[Helena Rubinstein]]. Faktorowicz created a line of cosmetics company in [[California]] known as [[Max Factor]] and coined the term "make-up" based on the verb phrase "to make up" one's face, now widely used as an alternative for describing cosmetics.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://kobieta.interia.pl/uroda/news-maks-faktorowicz-polak-ktory-stworzyl-kosmetyczne-imperium,nId,930672 |title=Maks Faktorowicz: Polak, który stworzył kosmetyczne imperium |language=pl |trans-title=Maks Faktorowicz: A Pole who created a cosmetic empire |website=Interia Kobieta |access-date=24 May 2017}}</ref> Faktorowicz also raised to fame by inventing modern [[eyelash extensions]] and by providing services to [[Hollywood]] artists.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.polskieradio.pl/10/501/Artykul/1245535,Maksymilian-Faktorowicz-czlowiek-ktory-dal-nam-sztuczne-rzesy |title=Maksymilian Faktorowicz – człowiek, który dał nam sztuczne rzęsy |language=pl |trans-title=Maksymilian Faktorowicz – a man who gave us false eyelashes |website=Polskie Radio |access-date=24 May 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |author=Stella Rose Saint Clair |url=https://www.beautylish.com/a/vxspr/the-history-of-max-factor |date=12 February 2014 |title=Makeup Masters: The History of Max Factor |website=Beautylish |access-date=24 May 2017}}</ref>

As of 2020, Poland possesses the fifth-largest cosmetic market in Europe.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.dailysabah.com/business/2019/05/22/poland-an-ambitious-player-making-a-name-in-the-cosmetics-industry|title=Poland: An ambitious player making a name in the cosmetics industry|first=Alen|last=Lepan|date=22 May 2019|website=Daily Sabah}}</ref><ref>https://www.polishcosmetics.pl/CATALOGUE_Cosmetics_Producers_from_Poland_for_US_Market.pdf</ref> Founded in 1983, [[Inglot Cosmetics]] is the country's largest beauty products manufacturer and retailer active in 700 locations worldwide, including retail salons in [[New York City]], [[London]], [[Milan]], [[Dubai]] and [[Las Vegas]].<ref>{{cite web |title=Przemyski Inglot ma już 400 sklepów na świecie |language=pl |trans-title=Przemysl Inglot already has 400 stores in the world |author=Norbert Ziętal |date=13 July 2013 |url=http://www.strefabiznesu.nowiny24.pl/artykul/przemyski-inglot-ma-juz-400-sklepow-na-swiecie |website=Strefa Biznesu}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://inglotcosmetics.com/about-us |title=About Us |publisher=Inglot Cosmetics |access-date=5 July 2017}}</ref> Established in 1999, the retail store [[Reserved]] is Poland's most successful clothing store chain, operating over 1,700 retail shops in 19 countries.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.retail-week.com/sectors/fashion/at-a-glance-polish-retailer-lpp-the-fashion-giant-nearing-a-uk-debut/7003956.article |url-access=subscription |title=At a glance: Polish retailer LPP, the fashion giant nearing a UK debut |author=Luke Tugby |date=18 January 2016 |website=Retail Week |access-date=9 September 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.hamburg-news.hamburg/en/cluster/trade-finances/polish-companies-highly-value-hamburg-their-expans/ |title=Polish Companies Highly Value Hamburg For Their Expansion Plans |work=Hamburg News |date=21 January 2015 |access-date=9 September 2016 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160829232654/http://www.hamburg-news.hamburg/en/cluster/trade-finances/polish-companies-highly-value-hamburg-their-expans/ |archive-date=29 August 2016 |url-status=dead }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.imagesretailme.com/2016/04/04/real-estate/polish-retailer-lpp-group-opens-largest-reserved-store-in-russia/ |website=Retail Me |title=Polish retailer LPP Group opens largest Reserved store in Russia |date=4 April 2016 |access-date=9 September 2016}}</ref> Internationally successful models from Poland include [[Anja Rubik]], [[Joanna Krupa]], [[Jac Jagaciak]], [[Kasia Struss]], [[Małgosia Bela]], and [[Magdalena Frąckowiak]].<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.trendrr.net/25843/most-beautiful-hottest-polish-women-best-famous-gorgeous/ |title= Top 10 Most Beautiful Polish Women |access-date=25 May 2019}}</ref>

===Cinema===
{{Main|Cinema of Poland|Theatre of Poland}}
[[File:Andrzej Wajda 1974.jpg|thumb|right|[[Andrzej Wajda]] was one of the greatest Polish film directors, and the recipient of a [[Honorary Oscar]], the [[Palme d'Or]], as well as Honorary [[Golden Lion]] and [[Golden Bear]] Awards.]]

The history of Polish cinema is as long as the history of [[cinematography]] itself. Over the decades, Poland has produced outstanding directors, film producers, cartoonists and actors that achieved world fame, especially in [[Hollywood]]. Moreover, Polish inventors played an important role in the development of world cinematography and modern-day television. Among the most famous directors and producers, who worked in Poland as well as abroad are [[Roman Polański]], [[Andrzej Wajda]], [[Samuel Goldwyn]], the [[Warner Brothers|Warner brothers]] ([[Harry Warner|Harry]], [[Albert Warner|Albert]], [[Sam Warner|Sam]], and [[Jack L. Warner|Jack]]), [[Max Fleischer]], [[Lee Strasberg]], [[Agnieszka Holland]] and [[Krzysztof Kieślowski]].<ref>{{cite book |last=Tzvetkova |first=Juliana |date=12 October 2017 |title=Pop Culture in Central Europe |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/Pop_Culture_in_Europe/Zk83DwAAQBAJ?hl=en&gbpv=0 |publisher=ABC-CLIO |page=188 |isbn=978-1-4408-4466-9}}</ref>

In the 19th century, throughout partitioned Poland, numerous amateur inventors, such as [[Kazimierz Prószyński]], were eager to construct a film projector. In 1894, Prószyński was successful in creating a [[Pleograph]], one of the first cameras in the world. The invention, which took photographs and projected pictures, was built before the [[Lumière brothers]] lodged their patent.<ref name="culture.pl">{{cite web|url=http://culture.pl/en/article/a-foreigners-guide-to-polish-cinema|title=A Foreigner's Guide to Polish Cinema |publisher=Culture.pl|access-date=6 April 2018}}</ref> He also patented an [[Aeroscope]], the first successful hand-held operated film camera. In 1897, [[Jan Szczepanik]], obtained a British patent for his [[Telectroscope]]. This prototype of television could easily transmit image and sound, thus allowing a live remote view.<ref name="culture.pl" />

Polish cinema developed rapidly in the [[interwar period]]. The most renowned star of the [[silent film]] era was Polish actress [[Pola Negri]]. During this time, the [[Yiddish cinema]] also evolved in Poland. Films in the [[Yiddish language]] with Jewish themes, such as ''[[The Dybbuk (film)|The Dybbuk]]'' (1937), played an important part in pre-war Polish cinematography. In 1945 the government established '[[Film Polski]]', a state-run film production and distribution organization, with director [[Aleksander Ford]] as the head of the company. Ford's ''[[Knights of the Teutonic Order (film)|Knights of the Teutonic Order]]'' (1960) was viewed by millions of people in the Soviet Union, Czechoslovakia and France.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.phil.muni.cz/dedur/?lang=1&id=964|title=Film Culture: Brno 1945–1970. The History of Distribution, Exhibition and Reception|website=www.phil.muni.cz|access-date=6 April 2018}}</ref> This success was followed by the historical films of [[Jerzy Hoffman]] and Andrzej Wajda. Wajda's 1975 film ''[[The Promised Land (1975 film)|The Promised Land]]'' was nominated at the [[48th Academy Awards]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://thequietus.com/articles/16644-the-promised-land-review|title=The Quietus – Film – Film Reviews – Peasant Company Excepted: Andrzej Wajda's The Promised Land|website=The Quietus|access-date=31 March 2019}}</ref>

In 2015, ''[[Ida (film)|Ida]]'' by [[Paweł Pawlikowski]] won the [[Academy Award for Best Foreign Language Film]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.newyorker.com/culture/culture-desk/ida-a-film-masterpiece|title="Ida": A Film Masterpiece|first=David|last=Denby|date=27 May 2014|access-date=6 April 2018|via=www.newyorker.com}}</ref> In 2019, Pawlikowski received an [[Academy Award for Best Director]] nomination for his historical drama ''[[Cold War (2018 film)|Cold War]]''. Other well-known Polish Oscar-winning productions include ''[[The Pianist (2002 film)|The Pianist]]'' (2002) by Roman Polański.<ref>{{cite book |last1=Stoddard |first1=Jeremy |last2=Marcus |first2=Alan S. |last3=Hicks |first3=David |date=26 June 2017 |title=Teaching Difficult History Through Film |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/Teaching_Difficult_History_through_Film/sAcqDwAAQBAJ?hl=en&gbpv=0 |page=188 |publisher=Taylor & Francis |isbn=978-1-317-27832-0}}</ref>

=== Media ===
{{Main|Television in Poland|Media of Poland}} {{further|Category:Video gaming in Poland}}
[[File:Siedziba Telewizji Polskiej w Warszawie 2017.jpg|left|thumb|Headquarters of the publicly funded national television network [[Telewizja Polska|TVP]] in Warsaw]]

Poland has a number of major media outlets, chief among which are the national television channels. [[Telewizja Polska|TVP]] is Poland's [[public broadcasting]] corporation; about a third of its income comes from a [[television licence|broadcast receiver licence]], while the rest is made through revenue from [[television advertisement|commercials]] and [[sponsor (commercial)|sponsorships]]. State television operates two mainstream channels, TVP 1 and TVP 2, as well as regional programs for each of the country's 16 [[voivodeship]]s (as [[TVP3|TVP 3]]). In addition to these general channels, TVP runs a number of genre-specific programmes such as [[TVP Sport]], [[TVP Historia]], [[TVP Kultura]], [[TVP Rozrywka]], [[TVP Seriale]] and [[TVP Polonia]], the latter is a state-run channel dedicated to the transmission of Polish language television for the [[Polish diaspora]]. Poland has several 24-hour news channels such as [[Polsat News]], [[TVP Info]] and [[TVN 24]].<ref>{{cite book |author=<!--Staff writer(s); no by-line.--> |title=The International Encyclopedia of Media Effects, 4 Volume Set |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/The_International_Encyclopedia_of_Media/w4_2DQAAQBAJ?hl=en&gbpv=0 |publisher=Wiley |page=1160 |date=6 March 2017 |isbn=978-1-118-78404-4}}</ref> Poland also possesses a variety of [[free-to-air]] television channels, chiefly [[TVN (Polish TV channel)|TVN]], [[Polsat]] and [[TV4 (Polish TV channel)|TV4]].

[[File:Podczas zawodów IEM (8464360471).jpg|thumb|right|[[Intel Extreme Masters]], an [[eSports]] video game tournament in [[Katowice]]]]

In Poland, there are also daily newspapers like ''[[Gazeta Wyborcza]]'' ("Electoral Gazette"), ''[[Rzeczpospolita (newspaper)|Rzeczpospolita]]'' ("The Republic") and ''[[Gazeta Polska Codziennie]]'' ("Polish Daily Newspaper") which provide traditional opinion and news, and [[tabloid (newspaper format)|tabloids]] such as ''[[Fakt]]'' and ''[[Super Express (newspaper)|Super Express]]''. Weeklies include ''[[Tygodnik Angora]]'', ''[[:pl:W Sieci|W Sieci]]'', ''[[Polityka]]'', ''[[Wprost]]'', ''[[Newsweek Polska]]'', ''[[Gość Niedzielny]]'' and ''[[Gazeta Polska]]''.<ref>{{cite book |last1=Bulandra |first1=Adam |last2=Kościółek |first2=Jakub |last3=Zimnoch |first3=Mateusz |date=2015 |title=Mowa nienawiści w przestrzeni publicznej |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/Mowa_nienawi%C5%9Bci_w_przestrzeni_publiczne/iFaaDwAAQBAJ?hl=en&gbpv=0 |language=pl |location=Poland |page=62 |publisher=Stowarzyszenie Interkulturalnipl |isbn=978-83-933307-5-1}}</ref>

Poland has also emerged as a major hub for video game developers in Europe, with the country now being home to hundreds of studios. Among the most successful ones are [[CD Projekt]], [[Techland]], [[CI Games]] and [[People Can Fly]].<ref>{{cite news|url=https://alumni.sae.edu/2015/03/02/polish-game-developers-its-time-to-get-to-know-them-better/ |title=Polish game developers: It's time to get to know them better! |access-date=7 September 2018}}</ref> Some of the most popular video games developed in Poland include [[The Witcher (video game series)|The Witcher]] trilogy.<ref>{{cite web |work=CNBC |date=14 October 2015 |title=Poland's video game sector powers up |author=Luke Graham |url=https://www.cnbc.com/2015/10/13/polands-video-game-sector-powers-up.html}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.scmp.com/lifestyle/arts-entertainment/article/1843073/how-poland-has-turned-video-game-powerhouse |title=How Poland turned into a video game powerhouse |access-date=7 September 2018}}</ref> [[Katowice]] hosts [[Intel Extreme Masters]], one of the biggest [[eSports]] events in the world.<ref>{{cite web |work=Fortune |date=3 March 2016 |title=Poland Is Home to the Biggest eSports Event in the World |url=http://fortune.com/2016/03/03/poland-is-home-to-the-biggest-esports-event-in-the-world/ |author=John Gaudiosi}}</ref>

=== Sports ===
{{Main|Sport in Poland}}
[[File:National Stadium Warsaw aerial view 2.jpg|thumb|upright=1.2|left|The [[Stadion Narodowy]] in Warsaw, home of the [[Poland national football team|national football team]], and one of the host stadiums of [[UEFA Euro 2012|Euro 2012]].]]
[[Volleyball]] and [[Association football]] are among the country's most popular sports, with a rich history of international competitions.<ref name="FIFA World Cup Statistics-Poland" /><ref name="FIFA Statistics – Poland" /> [[Track and field athletics|Track and field]], [[basketball]], [[handball]], boxing, [[Mixed martial arts|MMA]], [[motorcycle speedway]], [[ski jumping]], [[cross-country skiing (sport)|cross-country skiing]], [[ice hockey]], tennis, fencing, swimming, and [[Olympic weightlifting|weightlifting]] are other popular sports.

The golden era of [[football in Poland]] occurred throughout the 1970s and went on until the early 1980s when the [[Poland national football team|Polish national football team]] achieved their best results in any FIFA World Cup competitions finishing 3rd place in [[1974 FIFA World Cup|the 1974]] and [[1982 FIFA World Cup|the 1982]] tournaments. The team won a gold medal [[Football at the Summer Olympics|in football]] at the [[1972 Summer Olympics]] and two silver medals, [[1976 Summer Olympics|in 1976]] and [[1992 Summer Olympics|in 1992]]. In 2012, Poland co-hosted the [[UEFA Euro 2012|UEFA European Football Championship]].<ref name="warsaw-life" />

[[File:Derby Pomorza 2009 (Bydgoszcz).jpg|thumb|[[Motorcycle speedway]] (''żużel'')  racing is a very popular motorsport in Poland.<ref>Kevin Meynell & Marcin Babnis (7 July 2004), History of Polish Speedway. Main competitions. Rules. Retrieved 23 November 2020.</ref>]]

As of May 2021, the [[Poland men's national volleyball team|Polish men's national volleyball team]] is ranked [[FIVB World Rankings|as 2nd]] in the world.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.fivb.com/en/volleyball/rankings/seniorworldrankingmen|title=FIVB Senior World Ranking – Men |access-date=30 May 2021}}</ref> Volleyball team won a gold medal in [[Volleyball at the 1976 Summer Olympics – Men's tournament|Olympic 1976 Montreal]] and three gold medals in [[FIVB Volleyball Men's World Championship|FIVB World Championship]] [[1974 FIVB Volleyball Men's World Championship|1974]], [[2014 FIVB Volleyball Men's World Championship|2014]] and [[2018 FIVB Volleyball Men's World Championship|2018]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://poland2014.fivb.org/en|title=FIVB Volleyball Men's World Championship Poland 2014|access-date=1 January 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://italy-bulgaria2018.fivb.com/en/results-and-ranking/round4 |title=Finals |access-date=13 October 2018}}</ref>
[[Mariusz Pudzianowski]] is a highly successful strongman competitor and has won more [[World's Strongest Man]] titles than any other competitor in the world, winning the event in 2008 for the fifth time.<ref>{{cite book |last1=Fedor |first1=Dariusz |last2=Ramlau |first2=Łukasz |date=2009 |title=Polska, to tu się zaczęło |url=https://www.google.com.au/books/edition/Polska_to_tu_si%C4%99_zacz%C4%99%C5%82o/c94sAQAAIAAJ?hl=en&gbpv=0&bsq=kubica%202008%20grand%20prix%20do%20polski |language=pl |location=Poland |page=153 |publisher=Agora |isbn=978-83-7552-707-0}}</ref>

Poland has made a distinctive mark [[Speedway in Poland|in motorcycle speedway racing]] thanks to [[Tomasz Gollob]] and [[Bartosz Zmarzlik]], highly successful Polish riders. The top [[Speedway Ekstraliga|Ekstraliga]] division has one of [[List of attendance figures at domestic professional sports leagues#Outdoor|the highest average attendances]] for any sport in Poland. The [[Poland national speedway team|national speedway team of Poland]] is one of the major teams in international speedway.<ref name="Speedway World Cup: Poland win 2010 Speedway World Cup" />

Poles made significant achievements in mountaineering, in particular, in the [[Himalayas]] and the winter ascending of the [[eight-thousander]]s. Polish mountains are one of the tourist attractions of the country. Hiking, climbing, skiing and mountain biking and attract numerous tourists every year from all over the world.<ref name="turism" /> Water sports are the most popular summer recreation activities, with ample locations for fishing, canoeing, kayaking, sailing and windsurfing especially in the northern regions of the country.<ref>[http://www.polandforvisitors.com/travel_poland/summer_sports Summer Sports in Poland] at Poland For Visitors Online. Retrieved 2 November 2014.</ref>
